Witness Incompetence After Hadd Execution: Liability and Compensation
Ruling on witnesses found incompetent after hadd execution and liability for injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensating a convict when a witness is found incompetent after hadd execution, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
If witnesses are found incompetent after hadd execution, they are flogged for qadhf, and Abu Hanifa waives injury compensation to encourage testimony.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses a delicate scenario in hudud: when punishment has already been carried out but the testimony is later discovered defective. It clarifies the fate of the witnesses and discusses a key intra-Hanafi dispute on financial liability, focusing on the rule that the witnesses are flogged for qadhf and the differences between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn regarding compensation for injury and death, as well as liability upon retraction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Recognize that after hadd is executed based on four witnesses, if one is later found to be a slave or muhaddid, the remaining three witnesses are flogged for qadhf because their testimony is invalidated retroactively.
The initial ruling is clear: they are slanderers (qadhf) and must be punished.
2
Locate the dispute on compensation for injury
Note that Abu Hanifa says the compensation (arsh) for any injury caused by the flogging is waived (hdr), and if death occurs, the diya is from the public treasury. The Sahibayn hold that both arsh and diya are from the public treasury.
The dispute hinges on the nature of flogging: is it inherently injurious or not?
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil) of each party
The Sahibayn analogize flogging to rajm and qisas, where compensation for unintended harm comes from bayt al-mal because the act is attributed to the judge. Abu Hanifa differentiates: flogging is intended to be painful but not injurious or lethal; injury arises only from the flogger's error, so witnesses should not bear liability.
This is a qiyas for the Sahibayn; Abu Hanifa uses a more restricted definition of the prescribed punishment.
4
Extend the dispute to retraction and determine the mufta bihi
If the witnesses retract their testimony, Abu Hanifa holds they are not liable for compensation, while the Sahibayn hold they are. The text states the correct view (al-sahih) is that they are not liable, to avoid deterring people from testifying.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position, supported by policy consideration (sadd al-dhara'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولو حد فوجد أحدهم عبداً أو محدوداً (حدوا لأنهم قذفة إذ الشهود ثلاثة على ما بينا قوله : (وأرش ضربه هدر وإن فديته على بيت المال) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : أرش الضرب أيضاً على بيت المال ومعناه إذا كان جرحه، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا مات من الضرب وعلى هذا إذ رجع الشهود لا يضمنون عنده، وعندهما يضمنون. لهما أن الواجب بشهادتهم مطلق الضرب إذا الاحتراز عن الجرح خارج عن الوسع فينتظم الجارح وغيره فيضافان إلى شهادتهم فيضمنون بالرجوع وعند عدم الرجوع يجب على بيت المال لأنه ينتقل فعل الجلاد إلى القاضي وهو عامل للمسلمين فتجب الغرامة في مالهم وصار كالرجم والقصاص. ولأبي حنيفة أن الواجب هو الجلد وهو ضرب مؤلم غير جارح ولا مهلك ولا يقع جارحاً ظاهراً إلا لمعنى في الضارب وهو قلة هدايته فاقتصر عليه إلا أنه لا يجب الضمان عليه في الصحيح كيلا يمتنع الناس عن الإقامة مخافة الغرامة
His statement: (And if he is flogged and then one of them is found to be a slave or one who has received hadd, they are flogged because they are slanderers, since the witnesses are three as we explained. His statement: (And the compensation for his beating is waived, and his ransom is from the public treasury). This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the compensation for the beating is also from the public treasury. And its meaning is if he was wounded. And upon this disagreement if he dies from the beating. And upon this, if the witnesses retract, they are not liable according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them they are liable. Their argument: what is obligatory by their testimony is absolute beating; since avoiding injury is beyond capacity, the injury and non-injury are included, so they become liable upon retraction. In the absence of retraction, it is obligatory from the public treasury because the act of the flogger transfers to the judge, who is a worker for the Muslims, so the guarantee is due from their wealth, and it becomes like stoning (rajm) and qisas. And for Abu Hanifa: what is obligatory is flogging, which is a beating that is painful, not injuring or killing, and it does not appear as injuring externally except due to an attribute in the beater, namely his lack of skill. He restricted to that, but he does not guarantee it in the correct view, so that people are not prevented from establishing (testimony) for fear of guarantee.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses what happens if a hadd punishment (flogging) has already been executed based on the testimony of four witnesses, but afterwards one of the witnesses is found to be a slave or someone who has previously been punished with hadd (muhaddid). In such a case, the witnesses (now effectively three valid witnesses) are punished with hadd al-qadhf because they are slanderers. As for the compensation (arsh) for any injury caused during the flogging: there is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. According to Abu Hanifa, the compensation for injury (if the flogging caused wounds) is not to be paid by anyone (it is هدر, hdar), and the ransom (diya) if the person dies is from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the compensation for the beating (including injury) is also from the public treasury. The same dispute applies if the person dies from the beating. Furthermore, if the witnesses retract their testimony after the execution, Abu Hanifa holds that they are not liable to pay compensation, while the Sahibayn hold that they are liable. The Sahibayn argue that since the witnesses' testimony led to the beating, and injury is inevitable even if not intended, they should guarantee upon retraction. In the absence of retraction, the guarantee falls on the public treasury because the act is attributed to the judge. Abu Hanifa argues that the prescribed punishment (hadd) is flogging, which is defined as a painful strike that is not meant to injure or kill. If injury occurs, it is due to the flogger's error, not the witnesses' testimony. To avoid discouraging people from testifying, the witnesses are not held liable.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injury, determined by the extent of harm.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Muslims.
جلاد (jallad): The person who carries out the flogging (executioner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person is flogged based on testimony of four witnesses, and later one witness is found to be a slave, and the flogging causes injury, who pays the compensation for the injury?
A) The witnesses who falsely testified.
B) The flogger (jallad).
C) No compensation is paid; it is waived (hdr).
D) The public treasury (bayt al-mal).

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa waives injury compensation from witnesses to avoid deterring testimony, while the Sahibayn place it on the public treasury; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Retraction After Stoning: Witness Punished and Pays Diya
Ruling when one witness retracts after stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a witness retracts after stoning, explain the rationale (talil), and apply the distinction between direct and indirect causation.

Core Idea
Retraction turns testimony into slander: the witness is flogged and pays diya, not executed, because causation is indirect.

When a person is stoned to death based on four witnesses, and one witness later retracts, what happens to that witness? The Hanafi school holds that retraction annuls the testimony retroactively, turning it into slander (qadf). Consequently, the retracting witness must be punished for false accusation (hadd al-qadhf) and also compensate the deceased's heirs for the death he indirectly caused. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and clarifies why qisas (retaliation) is not applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What are the two consequences for the retracting witness? The text states 'حد وغرم ربع الدية' – he is flogged (80 lashes) and pays a quarter of the diya.
The hadd is for slander (qadf), not for murder.
2
Understand the dalil (proof)
Why does retraction trigger slander? Because the testimony is annulled retroactively, so the statement is now considered a false accusation against a dead person. The text says: 'لأن الشهادة انقلبت قذفاً بالرجوع'.
The analogy is to a direct slander: both are accusations of zina, but here the accused is dead.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (talil)
Why does the witness pay only a quarter of the diya? Because the other three witnesses stand by their testimony, so three-quarters of the right (blood) is upheld. The retractor's share of the loss is one-quarter.
The loss is apportioned based on the number of witnesses.
4
Examine the exception: no qisas
Why is the retractor not executed (qisas)? Because he caused the death indirectly (tasabbub), not directly (mubashara). Only direct killing triggers qisas.
The text emphasizes 'تسبب' vs 'مباشر'.
5
Contrast with the case of a slave witness
The restriction 'by retraction' indicates that if it becomes known that one witness was a slave, no one is punished because the testimony was invalid from the start, and all are considered slanderers.
This highlights the importance of timing: retraction after stoning annuls a previously valid judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو أحد لا ربعة بعد الرجم حد وغرم ربع (الدية لأن الشهادة انقلبت قذفاً بالرجوع لأن به تنفسخ الشهادة فجعل للحال قذفاً للميت وقد انفسخت الحجة فينفسخ ما ينبني عليه وهو القضاء في حقه فلا يورث الشبهة بخلاف ما إذا قذفه غيره لأنه غير محصن في حق غيره لقيام القضاء في حقه. وإنما غرم الواحد الراجع ربع الدية لبقاء من يبقى بشهادته ثلاثة أرباع الحق فيكون التالف بشهادة الراجع ربع الحق، ولا يجب القصاص على الراجع عندنا لأنه تسبب في الإتلاف وليس بمباشر قيد بالرجوع لأنه لو وجد واحد منهم عبداً فلا حد على واحد منهم لظهور أنها لم تكن شهادة بل هي قذف في ذلك الوقت فصاروا قاذفين حياً ثم يورث على ما سيجيء،
His statement: (So if one of the four retracts after stoning, he is flogged and pays a quarter of the diya) because the testimony turned into slander (qadf) by the retraction, because by it the testimony is annulled, so it is considered as slander of the dead person at that moment. And the proof has been annulled, so what is built upon it, namely the judgment against him, is annulled, so it does not leave a shubha. Unlike the case where someone else slanders him, because he is not muhsan (protected) in respect of others due to the existence of the judgment against him. And the one retracting pays only a quarter of the diya because by the remaining three, three-quarters of the right remains, so the loss caused by the testimony of the retractor is a quarter of the right. And qisas is not obligatory upon the retractor according to us because he caused the loss indirectly, not directly. He restricted to retraction because if one of them is found to be a slave, there is no hadd on any of them, because it becomes clear that it was not testimony but rather slander at that time, so they become slanderers while alive, then it will be inherited as will come.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the case where one of the four witnesses retracts his testimony after the accused has been stoned to death (rajm). The retracting witness is punished with hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes) and must pay a quarter of the diya (blood money) to the heirs of the deceased. The reason: the retraction annuls the testimony retroactively, so the testimony is now considered as a false accusation (qadf) against the deceased. However, unlike a normal qadf where the accused would be considered muhsan, here the person was already judged guilty and executed, so he is not muhsan in the sense that the slander alone would not subject the accuser to hadd? Actually the text says that because of the previous judgment, the deceased is not considered muhsan (protected) in relation to others, meaning if someone else slanders him after the judgment, they would not be punished because the judgment stands. But since the retraction annuls the judgment, the witness's retraction is treated as a new slander. The witness pays one-quarter of the diya because the remaining three witnesses' testimony continues to be valid, so three-quarters of the responsibility remains with them. The loss attributed to the retractor is one-quarter. The retractor is not subject to qisas (retaliation) because he only caused the death indirectly (tasabbub); direct killing (mubashara) is required for qisas. The author contrasts this with the case where one witness is found to be a slave after stoning: in that case, no one is punished for qadhf because the testimony was never valid (they were all considered slanderers from the start).

Key Terms
الدية (al-diya): Blood money paid to the heirs of a person wrongfully killed.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for zina when the convicted person is muhsan.
تسبب (tasabbub): Indirect causation, as opposed to direct causation (mubashara).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one of the four witnesses retracts after the accused is stoned, what punishment does the retracting witness face?
A) Qisas (execution) and payment of full diya.
B) Hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes) and payment of quarter of the diya.
C) Only hadd al-qadhf, no financial penalty.
D) Ta'zir punishment and no compensation.

Key Takeaway
A retracting witness is not executed because causation is indirect; he is flogged for slander and pays a quarter of the diya, with the amount determined by the number of remaining witnesses.

Retraction Before Execution: Witnesses Flogged, No Stoning
Ruling on witness retraction before execution of hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction before execution of hadd and explain the legal principle that doubt suspends the punishment.

Core Idea
Doubt repels the hadd: retraction before execution spares the accused and punishes the witnesses.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical moment in hudud cases: when witnesses withdraw their testimony before the punishment is carried out. The ruling demonstrates the Hanafi principle that hudud are suspended by doubts (shubuhat). We will explore the consequences for both the witnesses and the accused, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Retraction of testimony occurs BEFORE the hadd (stoning) is executed. The accused has not yet been punished.
Timing is crucial: retraction after execution has a different ruling.
2
Determine the ruling for the witnesses
The witnesses are punished with hadd al-qadhf (flogging) for false testimony. The text says 'حدوا' (they are flogged).
This is because their retraction effectively admits they previously gave false testimony.
3
Determine the ruling for the accused
The accused is not stoned. The text says 'ولا رجم' (no stoning). The hadd is dropped due to the doubt created by the retraction.
Hudud are repelled by uncertainties; the retraction introduces a shubha.
4
Understand the legal principle
The retraction casts doubt on the certainty required for execution. The Hanafi principle 'الحدود تدرأ بالشبهات' (hudud are repelled by doubts) applies here.
This principle is derived from the Prophet's hadith: 'ادرأوا الحدود بالشبهات'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقبله حدوا ولا رجم) أي لو مات والحد لا
His statement: (And before it they are flogged and there is no stoning) meaning if he dies and the hadd does not...
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This brief passage states the ruling for retraction before the hadd (stoning) is carried out. If one or more of the witnesses retract before the accused is executed, the witnesses are punished with hadd al-qadhf (flogging), and the accused is not stoned. The stoning is suspended because the retraction creates a doubt (shubha) that prevents the execution. This is consistent with the principle that hudud are repelled by doubts. The text is incomplete in the OCR but the ruling is clear from the context and other Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony by a witness.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or uncertainty that repels the application of hadd punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the witnesses retract their testimony before the accused is stoned?
A) The accused is stoned anyway and the witnesses are punished.
B) The accused is not stoned and the witnesses are flogged.
C) Both the accused and witnesses are punished.
D) The charges are dropped and no one is punished.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of testimony before execution of hadd results in flogging of the witnesses and suspension of the stoning due to the doubt created.

Witness Incompetency After Hadd and Liability for Arsh
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on witness incompetency after hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling when witnesses are found incompetent after hadd and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and Sahibayn's positions on liability for arsh upon retraction.

Core Idea
Witnesses found incompetent after hadd are punished for qadhf, but liability for injury from flogging is disputed: Abu Hanifa denies arsh; Sahibayn affirm it upon retraction.

Imagine that after a hadd punishment for zina is carried out, it is discovered that one of the witnesses was a slave or had previously been punished for false accusation (qadhf). What happens to the witnesses and to any compensation for injury from the flogging? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether the witnesses must pay compensation (arsh) if they retract after the flogging caused injury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and basic ruling
Note that after the hadd is executed, it is discovered that one witness was a slave or a maḥdūd (punished for qadhf). The ruling: all witnesses are punished for qadhf (80 lashes), arsh for injury is wasted (hadr), and if stoning/death occurs, diya is paid from Bayt al-Mal.
The key is that the witnesses are treated as false accusers (qudhāt) because their collective testimony was defective.
2
Recognize the point of dispute
The dispute arises when the witnesses retract their testimony after the flogging that caused injury. The question is: are they liable to pay arsh (compensation) for the injury?
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on this point.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the witnesses are not liable for arsh. His proof: the prescribed punishment (jald) is a painful but non-injurious beating; any injury is due to the executioner's error, not the testimony.
He also argues that imposing liability would discourage people from carrying out punishments.
4
Analyze Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the witnesses are liable for arsh upon retraction. Their proof: the required flogging inherently risks injury; since avoiding injury is beyond capacity, the injury is attributed to the witnesses' testimony. If no retraction, Bayt al-Mal pays because the executioner acts for the state.
They analogize to stoning or qisas where compensation is from Bayt al-Mal.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is clear: if witnesses retract after injurious flogging, in Abu Hanifa's view they pay nothing; in Sahibayn's view they must pay arsh. If they do not retract, both agree Bayt al-Mal pays.
No tarjih is provided in this text, so both positions remain valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الزنا والرجوع عنها المشهود عليهما ولو حد فوجد أحدهم عبداً أو محدوداً حدوا وأرش ضربه هدر وإن فديته على بيت المال . قوله : ( ولو حد فوجد أحدهم عبداً أو محدوداً (حدوا لأنهم قذفة إذ الشهود ثلاثة على ما بينا قوله : (وأرش ضربه هدر وإن رجم فديته على بيت المال) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : أرش الضرب أيضاً على بيت المال ومعناه إذا كان جرحه، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا مات من الضرب وعلى هذا إذ رجع الشهود لا يضمنون عنده، وعندهما يضمنون. لهما أن الواجب بشهادتهم مطلق الضرب إذا الاحتراز عن الجرح خارج عن الوسع فينتظم الجارح وغيره فيضافان إلى شهادتهم فيضمنون بالرجوع وعند عدم الرجوع يجب على بيت المال لأنه ينتقل فعل الجلاد إلى القاضي وهو عامل للمسلمين فتجب الغرامة في مالهم وصار كالرجم والقصاص. ولأبي حنيفة أن الواجب هو الجلد وهو ضرب مؤلم غير جارح ولا مهلك ولا يقع جارحاً ظاهراً إلا لمعنى في الضارب وهو قلة هدايته فاقتصر عليه إلا أنه لا يجب الضمان عليه في الصحيح كيلا يمتنع الناس عن الإقامة مخافة الغرامة
The two persons against whom testimony is given, and if they are punished, then one of them is found to be a slave or previously punished, they are all punished, and the compensation for his beating is wasted, and if he is stoned, his blood money is upon the treasury.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling states that if after executing the hadd punishment (flogging) for zina, it is discovered that one of the witnesses was a slave (disqualified from testifying in hadd cases) or had been previously punished for qadhf (false accusation), then all witnesses are punished for qadhf (80 lashes) because their testimony is essentially qadhf. The compensation (arsh) for any injury caused by the flogging is not recoverable (hadr); however, if the accused dies from the flogging, the diya (blood money) is paid from the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal). The dispute arises when the witnesses retract their testimony after the flogging. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the witnesses are not liable for the arsh if they retract because the prescribed flogging is intended to be non-injurious; any injury is due to the executioner's error. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), the witnesses are liable for the arsh upon retraction because the flogging inherently risks injury, and if no retraction, the Bayt al-Mal pays because the executioner acts for the state. The passage provides proofs for both positions: the two companions argue that since avoiding injury is impossible, the injury is attributed to the witnesses' testimony; Abu Hanifa argues that the prescribed punishment is merely painful beating, not injurious, so liability would discourage people from carrying out punishments.

Key Terms
محدود (maḥdūd): A person who has been punished for qadhf (false accusation of zina), thus disqualified from testifying in hadd cases.
أرش الضرب (arsh al-ḍarb): Compensation (diya) for injury caused by flogging, beyond the prescribed punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn regarding arsh after flogging injury?
A) Whether the flogging was prescribed or not.
B) Whether the prescribed flogging is inherently non-injurious or carries risk of injury.
C) Whether the witnesses retracted before or after the flogging.
D) Whether the executioner is liable instead.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses are found incompetent after hadd, they are punished for qadhf, and liability for injury from flogging upon retraction is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa denies arsh; Sahibayn affirm it.

Retraction of a Witness in a Hadd Case: Effects on Punishment and Liability
Rulings on effects of witness retraction in zina cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of one witness in a zina case and apply the distinction between retraction before and after execution of punishment.

Core Idea
A witness who retracts after rajm is punished for qadhf and pays quarter diya; retraction before rajm nullifies the testimony for all.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the consequences when one of the four witnesses in a zina case retracts his testimony. The ruling depends critically on whether the punishment has been executed (rajm or jald) or not. Understanding this distinction reveals how Hanafi jurists balance the integrity of testimony with the rights of the accused and the retracting witness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Separate the case of retraction after rajm from retraction before rajm. Note the different rulings: after rajm, the retractor alone is punished and pays quarter diya; before rajm, all four witnesses are punished and rajm is not carried out.
Also note the case of flogging (jald) which is simpler and agreed upon.
2
Analyze the rationale for after rajm
Understand why only the retractor is liable: his testimony caused a quarter of the death (since four witnesses each cause an equal share). The death is already executed, so it cannot be undone, but the retraction converts his testimony into qadhf. Therefore he faces hadd for qadhf and must compensate for his share of the diya.
The principle: 'al-shahadah inqalabat qadhfan' (the testimony becomes qadhf).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on retraction after judgment but before execution
Compare the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (all witnesses punished) with Muhammad (only retractor punished). The key point is whether the judgment is considered final before execution. The majority holds that execution is necessary to finalize the ruling; without it, the testimony is still inchoate.
Zufar also holds that even before judgment, only the retractor is punished — but this is against the three.
4
Apply the underlying principle
The passage states 'kalamuhum qadhf fi al-asl' — their words are originally qadhf. Testimony becomes valid only by being connected to the ruling (ittisal al-qada). Retraction before execution breaks this connection, reverting the testimony to qadhf for all witnesses. After execution, the connection is severed only for the retractor.
This principle also explains why retraction after flogging only punishes the retractor by consensus.
5
Extend to other scenarios
What if all four retract? They all are punished and each pays a quarter of diya. What if the witnesses include a slave? There is no hadd for any because the testimony was invalid from the start. These extensions are covered in the passage.
The passage also hints at inheritance implications later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو رجع أحد الأربعة بعد الرجم حد وغرم ربع الدية وقبله رجم . قوله : (فلو أحد لا ربعة بعد الرجم حد وغرم ربع (الدية لأن الشهادة انقلبت قذفاً بالرجوع لأن به تنفسخ الشهادة فجعل للحال قذفاً للميت وقد انفسخت الحجة فينفسخ ما ينبني عليه وهو القضاء في حقه فلا يورث الشبهة بخلاف ما إذا قذفه غيره لأنه غير محصن في حق غيره لقيام القضاء في حقه. وإنما غرم الواحد الراجع ربع الدية لبقاء من يبقى بشهادته ثلاثة أرباع الحق فيكون التالف بشهادته الراجع ربع الحق، ولا يجب القصاص على الراجع عندنا لأنه تسبب في الإتلاف وليس بمباشر قيد بالرجوع لأنه لو وجد واحد منهم عبداً فلا حد على واحد منهم لظهور أنها لم تكن شهادة بل هي قذف في ذلك الوقت فصاروا قاذفين حياً ثم يورث على ما سيجيء، ء، وأشار إلى أنه لو كان حده الجلد فجلد بشهادتهم ثم رجع واحد منهم فإنه يحد الراجع بالأولى وهو متفق عليه وفي مسألة الكتاب خلاف زفر، وإلى أنه لو رجع الكل حدوا وغرموا ربع الدية وإلى أنه لو شهد على رجل أربعة أنه زنى بفلانة وشهد عليه أربعة آخرون بالزنا بغيرها ورجم فرجع الفريقان فإنهم يضمنون الدية إجماعاً ويحدون للقذف عندهما. وقال محمد : لا يحدون قوله : (وقبله حدوا ولا رجم) أي لو رجع أحدهم قبل الرجم حد الكل الراجع وغيره وامتنع الرجم. وقال محمد: حد الراجع خاصة لأن الشهادة تأكدت بالقضاء فلا ينفسخ إلا في حق الراجع كما إذا رجع بعد الإمضاء ولهما إن الإمضاء من القضاء وصار كما إذا رجع واحد منهم قبل القضاء ولهذا يسقط الحد عن المشهود عليه . أطلق في قوله «قبله فشمل ما إذا كان قبل القضاء أو بعده، وخلاف محمد إنما هو فيما بعد القضاء، وأما قبل القضاء فيحد الكل عند الثلاثة خلافاً لزفر فإنه قال : يحد الراجع خاصة لأنه لا يصدق على غيره ولنا أن كلامهم قذف في الأصل وإنما يصير شهادة باتصال القضاء به فإذا لم يتصل بقي قذفاً فيحدون
If one of the four retracts after the stoning, he is punished and pays a quarter of the blood money; before it, they are all punished and no stoning.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage explains the consequences when one of the four witnesses in a zina case retracts his testimony. If the retraction occurs after the accused has been stoned to death (rajm), the retracting witness is punished for qadhf (80 lashes) and must pay a quarter of the diya (blood money) because his testimony was the cause of a quarter of the death. If the retraction occurs before the punishment is executed, then all four witnesses are punished for qadhf and the stoning is not carried out. The commentary clarifies that the testimony is essentially qadhf from the beginning; it only becomes valid testimony through connection to the judge's ruling. If the ruling has been executed (rajm), retraction only affects the retractor. If the ruling has not been executed, retraction breaks the connection and all are considered qadhf. There is a difference of opinion: Imam Muhammad holds that if retraction occurs after judgment but before execution, only the retractor is punished; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that all are punished because the judgment is not yet final. The passage also discusses cases of flogging (jald) where retraction leads to punishment of the retractor by consensus.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujūʿ): Retraction of testimony by a witness after it has been given.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; a hadd crime punishable by 80 lashes.
دية (diya): Blood money paid to the victim's family in cases of homicide or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a witness retracts after the accused has been stoned to death, what happens?
A) The witness is not punished but must pay full diya
B) The witness is punished for qadhf and pays a quarter of diya
C) All witnesses are punished and no further action
D) The witness is only punished for qadhf without financial liability

Key Takeaway
The timing of retraction determines whether only the retractor or all witnesses are liable for qadhf and whether the punishment stands.

Retraction by Fifth Witness and Liability of Muzakki
Rulings on retraction by additional witnesses and liability of credibility verifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on retraction of additional witnesses in a hadd case and distinguish when muzakki are liable for diya according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
One extra witness can retract freely; when the number falls below four, retractors face hadd and fractional diya; muzakki are liable if they retract knowingly.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two distinct but related liability issues in hudud cases. First, when there are five witnesses for zina, the retraction of one carries no penalty because the remaining four still suffice. However, if a second retracts, the two retractors are punished for qadhf and must pay a quarter of the diya each. Second, if it later emerges that the witnesses were slaves (hence disqualified), the credibility verifiers (muzakki) are liable for the full diya per Abu Hanifa if they retract and admit deliberate lying, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad place the burden on the Bayt al-Mal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness count scenario
Note that the case involves five witnesses for a hadd crime (zina). If one retracts, four remain. If a second retracts, only three remain, which is insufficient for the hadd.
The number four is key: testimony of four free, just males is required for zina hadd (Quran 24:13).
2
Apply the ruling for one retraction
When only one of the five retracts, there is no liability on him because the remaining four witnesses carry the full right to the hadd punishment. The retractor is exempt from both hadd (qadhf) and diya.
This holds whether retraction occurs before or after execution of the hadd.
3
Apply the ruling for a second retraction
If a second witness retracts, the two retractors are each punished for qadhf and must pay one quarter of the diya. The total diya is split equally among them because each contributed to the loss of life by their false testimony.
The fraction is based on the share of the right each retractor's testimony represented.
4
Analyze the muzakki liability dispute
When witnesses are later found to be slaves (disqualified), the muzakki (those who vouched for their credibility) may be liable. Trace Abu Hanifa's reasoning: tazkiya is the cause of the cause (illat al-illa) for the testimony's acceptance, so the diya is attributed to them if they retract and admit deliberate falsehood.
Sahibayn analogize to praising the victim (ihsan), which is a mere condition, not a cause, so liability falls on Bayt al-Mal.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text does not explicitly give a tarjih. Note that the dispute is within the Hanafi school, and the practical difference (thamarah) is who pays the diya: the muzakki or the public treasury.
In practice, following Abu Hanifa may be stricter, while Sahibayn's view is more protective of the verifiers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (و لو أحد الخمسة لا شيء عليه لأنه بقي من يبقى بشهادته كل الحق وهو شهادة الأربع، وشمل قوله «لا شيء عليه الحد والغرم وما إذا كان قبل القضاء وبعده، وأفاد أنه لا شيء على الأربعة بالأولى، وحاصله أنه لا شيء على الكل وكأنه لم يرجع أحد . رجع الثالث قوله : (فإن رجع آخر حداً وغرما ربع (الدية أما الحد فلانفساخ القضاء بالرجم في حقهما، وأما الغرامة فلأنه بقي من يبقى بشهادته ثلاثة أرباع الحق والمعتبر بقاء من بقي على ما عرف. وأفاد بالغرامة أن المسألة بعد الرجم لأنه لو كان قبله فلا غرامة وإنما لزم الأول برجوع الثاني لأنه وجد منه الموجب للحد والضمان وهو قذفه وإتلافه بشهادته وإنما امتنع الوجوب لمانع وهو بقاء من يقوم بالحق، فإذا زال المانع برجوع الثاني ظهر الوجوب، وإذا رجع ضمن ربع الدية، وكذا الثاني والأول، وإذا رجع الخمسة ضمنوا الدية أخماساً؛ كذا في الحاوي القدسي قوله : ( وضمن المزكون دية المرجوم إن ظهروا عبيداً) يعني ضمن المزكون برجوعهم عن التزكية دية المرجوم إن ظهر الشهود أنهم ليسوا أهلاً للشهادة عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : هي على بيت المال لأنهم أثنوا على الشهود خيراً فصار كما إذا أثنوا على المشهود عليه خيراً بأن شهدوا بإحصانه. وله أن الشهادة إنما تصير حجة وعاملة بالتزكية فكانت التزكية في معنى علة العلة فيضاف الحكم إليها بخلاف شهود الإحصان لأنه محض الشرط قيدنا بكونهم رجعوا بأن قالوا تعمدنا الكذب مع علمنا بأنهم ليسوا أحراراً لأنهم لو ثبتوا على تزكيتهم ولم يرجعوا أو قالوا أخطأنا لم يضمنوا بالإجماع لأنهم أخطؤوا فيما عملوا لعامة المسلمين فصاروا كالقاضي. وأفاد بالمزكين أنهم أخبروا بحرية الشهود وإسلامهم وعدالتهم لتكون تزكية، سواء كان بلفظ الشهادة أو بلفظ الإخبار، لأنهم لو أخبروا بأنهم عدول ثم ظهروا عبيداً لم يضمنوا اتفاقاً لأنها ليست تزكية، والقاضي قد أخطأ حيث اكتفى بهذا القدر. وقيد بالمزكيين لأنه لا ضمان على الشهود والمسألة بحالها لأن كلامهم لم يقع شهادة ولا يحدون للقذف لأنهم قذفوا حياً وقد مات فلا الرملي : صوابه جميع الدية. قال في النهر بعد قوله وغرم ربع الدية لأن الذي تلف بشهادته إنما هو ربع الحق ولذا لو رجع الكل حدوا وغرموا الدية اهـ.
If one of the five retracts, nothing is against him because there remain four whose testimony carries full right. If a second retracts, they are punished and pay a quarter of diya... And the verifiers (muzakki) are liable for the diya of the stoned person if they turn out to be slaves, according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct scenarios. First, if there are five witnesses (one extra) and one retracts, there is no liability on him because the remaining four witnesses still suffice for the capital punishment. However, if a second witness also retracts, then the two retractors are punished for qadhf and each pays a quarter of the diya (total half), because only two witnesses remain, insufficient for punishment. Second, the passage discusses the liability of those who testified to the credibility of the witnesses (muzakki). If after the punishment it is discovered that the witnesses were slaves (hence disqualified), the muzakki are liable for the diya if they retract their verification and admit they knowingly lied. According to Abu Hanifa, they must pay the diya because their verification was the effective cause (illat al-illa) for accepting the testimony. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the diya is on the Bayt al-Mal because the muzakki merely gave an opinion, and the judge erred. If the muzakki do not retract or claim error, they are not liable by consensus. The passage also clarifies that the term 'muzakki' only applies if they explicitly testified to the witnesses' freedom and reliability; mere information does not incur liability.

Key Terms
مزكون (muzakkūn): Persons who testify to the credibility (freedom, Islam, 'adala) of witnesses in a hadd case.
تزكية (tazkiya): The act of vouching for a witness's credibility, specifically testifying to their freedom, Islam, and 'adala.
علة العلة (illat al-illa): Cause of the cause; a secondary effective cause that is close to the primary cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when are muzakki liable for the diya of the stoned person?
A) Whenever the witnesses turn out to be slaves.
B) Only if they retract their verification and admit they deliberately lied knowing the witnesses were not free.
C) Only if they retract after the punishment, regardless of their intent.
D) They are never liable because they are not witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, liability in hadd cases depends on the number of credible witnesses and the nature of the credibility verification; extra witnesses and verifiers are accountable only when their actions directly cause the loss of right.

Liability of Witness Certifiers Only Upon Retraction
Correcting a common misconception about liability of witness certifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability of witness certifiers (muzakkun) and explain why retraction is the sole cause of liability, distinguishing it from the discovery of witnesses' unfitness.

Core Idea
Liability of witness certifiers arises only upon their retraction — not from the witnesses' unfitness alone.

Many earlier Hanafi texts mistakenly treated the unworthiness of witnesses as a separate ground for liability on those who certified them. In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq corrects this error, clarifying the precise cause (sabab) of liability. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper application of liability in hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act of the muzakkun (certifying witnesses) and the ruling on their liability. Determine what triggers the liability.
The ruling is that liability (daman) for diyah becomes wajib on the muzakkun only under specific conditions.
2
Distinguish two scenarios
Contrast the scenario where witnesses are found to be unqualified (e.g., slaves) from the scenario where the certifiers themselves retract their certification.
Many texts treat both as causes, but the author distinguishes them.
3
Identify the correct cause
Recognize that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the only cause for liability is retraction by the certifiers. The witnesses' unfitness alone does not impose liability.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Determine the consequence when there is no retraction
If the certifiers do not retract but the witnesses are found unqualified, the diyah is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) by agreement.
This shows the default liability falls on the state, not the certifiers.
5
Recognize the correction
Note that the author corrects a prevalent error in earlier texts (e.g., in Al-Mabsut and the poem) that suggested two separate grounds for liability.
The correction reinforces the principle that liability follows directly from the act that invalidates the judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله إن ظهروا عبيداً مثال بل المراد أن ظهر أنهم ليسوا أهلاً للشهادة ولو كانوا كفاراً. ثم اعلم أنه وقع في كثير من الكتب وجوب الضمان على المزكين بظهورهم عبيداً من غير تقييد برجوع المزكين حتى جعلها في المنظومة مسألتين: المسألة الأولى فيما إذا ظهروا عبيداً. الثانية إذا رجع المزكون وليس الأمر كذلك. والحاصل أن ظهور الشهود عبيداً وعدمه لا تأثير له في ضمان المزكين وإنما الموجب عليهم هو الرجوع فقط عند الإمام، وإذا لم يرجعوا وظهروا عبيداً فالضمان في بيت المال اتفاقاً.
And his statement: 'If they appear as slaves' is an example, rather the meaning is that it appears that they are not qualified for testimony, even if they were disbelievers. Then know that many books mention the obligation of liability on the certifiers (muzakkun) due to the witnesses appearing as slaves without restricting it to the retraction of the certifiers, so that they made it in the poem two issues: the first issue when they appear as slaves, the second when the certifiers retract, but it is not like that. The upshot is that the appearance of the witnesses as slaves or not has no effect on the liability of the certifiers; rather what necessitates liability upon them is only retraction according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And if they do not retract and the witnesses appear as slaves, the liability is upon the public treasury (bayt al-mal) by agreement.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expansion clarifying the ruling on the liability of those who certify the integrity of witnesses (muzakkun) in zina cases. The author states that many earlier texts mistakenly believed that the certifiers are liable if the witnesses are later found to be slaves (i.e., unqualified). The author corrects this: the certifiers are liable only if they themselves retract their certification. If they do not retract and the witnesses turn out to be unqualified, then the diyah is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal), not from the certifiers. This is the Hanafi position as held by Imam Abu Hanifa and agreed upon by the later scholars. The ruling is based on the principle that retraction invalidates the basis of the judgment, leading to liability.

Key Terms
المزكين (al-muzakkūn): Those who certify the uprightness ('adalah) of witnesses before the judge.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Financial liability, here specifically for the diyah (blood money) of the wrongfully executed person.
بيت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Muslim state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The witnesses being found to be slaves.
B) The witnesses being found to be disbelievers.
C) The certifiers retracting their certification.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
The certifiers of witnesses are liable for diyah only if they retract their certification; otherwise, diyah is from the public treasury.

Witnesses Deliberately Looking at Private Parts for Testimony
Ruling on permissibility of zina witnesses looking at private parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zina witnesses looking at private parts and explain the analogical basis for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Zina witnesses may look at private parts out of necessity, analogized to medical treatment.

This passage from Bahar al-Ra'iq discusses a specific exception to the general prohibition of looking at 'awrah. The author explains that witnesses of zina, who must observe the act of penetration to testify, are permitted to look at the private parts out of necessity, drawing an analogy to physicians and other professionals. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the qiyas (analogy) that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Determine what act is being ruled upon and the specific condition that triggers the exception.
The act is looking at 'awrah; the condition is necessity for testimony.
2
Understand the general prohibition
Recognize that looking at a non-mahram's 'awrah is normally haram. The exception is based on darurah (necessity).
3
Recognize the exception for necessity
Identify the specific necessity: witnesses must see penetration (dukhul) to fulfill the shahada requirement.
Hanafis require four male witnesses to have seen the act itself.
4
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) to other cases
The author analogizes witnesses to physicians, midwives, circumcisers, etc. Identify the illa (effective cause) as 'necessity without lust'.
The common factor is a valid shari'i need that overrides the general prohibition.
5
Note the restriction of no suspicious intent
The permission is conditional on the witnesses not having a 'suspicious intent' (qasd mureeb).
If they looked for lust, it would be haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن قال شهود الزنا تعمدنا النظر قبل شهادتهم لأنه يباح النظر لهم إلى الفرج ضرورة تحمل الشهادة فأشبه الطبيب والقابلة والخافضة والختان والإحتقان والبكارة في العنة) قوله : (فأشبه الطبيب الخ ذكر المواضع التي يباح فيها النظر إلى العورة عند العذر وقد نظمتها: بقولي: ولا تنظر لعورة أجنبي. بلا عذر كقابلة طبيب وختان وخافضة وحقن شهود زنا بلا قصد مريب وعلم بكارة في عنة أو زنا أو حين . رد للمعيب.
His statement: (And if the witnesses of zina say: We deliberately looked before our testimony) because looking at the private part is permitted for them due to necessity of undertaking testimony, so it is similar to the physician, the midwife, the circumciser, the cupper, the one who administers enema, and the examination of virginity in case of impotence. His statement: (so it is similar to the physician, etc.) mentions the places where looking at the private part is permitted due to an excuse. And I have versified it: 'And do not look at the private part of a non-mahram without an excuse, like a midwife, physician, circumciser, cupper, enema administrator, or zina witnesses without suspicious intent, and knowledge of virginity in case of impotence or zina or then. Return for the defective.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that witnesses of zina may deliberately look at the private parts of the accused in order to witness the act of penetration. The author explains that this is permissible out of necessity, similar to how a physician or midwife may look at the private parts for medical treatment. The poem summarizes all such cases: looking at the private part of a non-mahram is prohibited without an excuse, but excuses include medical needs (physician, midwife, circumciser, cupper, enema), and for zina witnesses if they are not suspect, and for examining virginity in cases of impotence or accusation of zina. The key point is that the witnesses' looking is only permissible if done with a legitimate purpose (shahada), not for lust.

Key Terms
العورة (al-ʻawrah): Private parts that must be covered and are normally prohibited to look at.
الشهادة (al-shahādah): Testimony; here specifically for zina, requiring witnessing of actual penetration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if they are physicians.
B) Only out of necessity for testimony and without suspicious intent.
C) They cannot look under any circumstances.
D) Only if the accused consents.

Key Takeaway
Looking at 'awrah is generally haram, but becomes permissible when necessary for fulfilling a legitimate legal duty, as in zina testimony or medical treatment.

Accepting Women's Testimony for Ihsan: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on accepting one man and two women's testimony for ihsan, with sub-issues on birth evidence and wording of testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting one man and two women's testimony for ihsan, distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Zufar positions, and apply the Hanafi qiyas in support.

Core Idea
Ihsan is a condition, not a penalty, so women's testimony is accepted to prove it—a key Hanafi distinction.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the Hanafi school defends its ruling that the testimony of one man and two women suffices to prove a person is muhsan (subject to stoning). This places ihsan in a different category than the actual hadd penalty. The commentary explains the reasoning and refutes the objections of al-Shafi'i and Zufar. It also addresses intra-Hanafi differences on the wording of testimony and the effect of a child's birth.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the testimony of one man and two women is accepted to prove ihsan. Also note that the birth of a child from the accused's wife suffices.
The matn states: 'If he denies ihsan, then one man and two women testify against him, or his wife gives birth from him, he is stoned.'
2
Identify the opposing schools and their proofs
Al-Shafi'i rejects women's testimony in non-financial matters. Zufar treats ihsan as an effective cause ('illa) for stoning, so he rejects women's testimony to avert the penalty.
Zufar analogizes ihsan to manumission of a slave before zina, where women's testimony is also rejected.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that ihsan is not an 'illa but a set of conditions (praiseworthy characteristics) that prevent zina. It is not a penal element itself, so the analogy with financial matters or manumission is flawed.
The difference with manumission is that there is no contradictory here to necessitate strict proof.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a muhsan can be stoned based on such evidence; under Shafi'i/Zufar, the penalty would be averted due to insufficient proof of ihsan.
This affects the application of hadd penalties in practice.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on wording of testimony
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept the phrase 'dakhala biha' (entered with her) as sufficient proof of intercourse, but Muhammad al-Shaybani requires explicit mention of union (jama' or bada').
This is a secondary dispute within the school; the mufta bihi is the more lenient view.

Their testimony is accepted. And if he denies ihsan, then one man and two women testify against him, or his wife gives birth from him, he is stoned. (And if he denies ihsan, and one man and two women testify against him, or his wife gives birth from him, he is stoned) i.e., if he denies the entry (dukhul) after the existence of other conditions. As for if she gives birth from him, because the ruling of establishing lineage from him is a ruling of entry upon him, and for this reason if he divorces her, he retains the right to take her back, and ihsan is established by such evidence. As for when one man and two women testify against him concerning ihsan after he denied some of its conditions like marriage, entry, or freedom, it is contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Al-Shafi'i is upon his principle that their testimony is not accepted in other than financial matters. Zufar says it is a condition in the sense of the 'illa (effective cause) because the crime is aggravated in his view, so the ruling is attached to it, resembling the true 'illa, so women's testimony is not accepted therein as a precaution to avert the penalty, and it becomes like when two dhimmis testify against a dhimmi that he committed zina with a Muslim slave woman whom he freed before the zina, it is not accepted for what we mentioned. Our proof is that ihsan is composed of praiseworthy characteristics and they prevent from zina as mentioned, so it is not in the sense of an 'illa. And it becomes as if they testified about it in other than this case. And it is not that it is retraction of an acknowledgment, so it indicates that it is like the hadd. We say: It is only valid because there is no one to contradict him in it, unlike what was mentioned because manumission is established by their testimony, but the precedence of date is not established because the Muslim denies it and the Muslim is harmed by it. They said: The manner of testimony for entry is that the witnesses say: He married a woman and had intercourse with her (jama'aha or bada'aha). If they say 'he entered with her' (dakhala biha), it suffices according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: It does not suffice and his ihsan is not established by that because 'dakhala' is shared between intercourse, wedding procession, seclusion, and visiting, so it is not established due to doubt, like the words 'qurban' and 'ityan'. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that when it is attributed to the woman with the letter ba' (bi), it is specific for intercourse, unlike 'dakhala 'alayha' which is for visiting. If he secluded with her and then divorced her and said 'I had intercourse with her' and she denied, he becomes muhsan but she does not. Similarly, if after divorce she said 'I was Christian' and he said 'she was Muslim'. When one of the two adulterers is muhsan, each is punished with his appropriate hadd. If the witnesses of ihsan retract, they do not guarantee, and it is well-known. In al-Muhit: If a man's wife acknowledges that she is his mother, then the man commits zina, he is stoned. If she acknowledges being a slave before he enters with her, then he commits zina, he is not stoned by istihsan, not by qiyas. A man married a woman without a guardian and entered with her; Abu Yusuf said: They are not muhsan by that because this marriage is definitely invalid due to the disagreement of scholars and the information about it. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage deals with proving ihsan (the condition that makes a person muhsan and subject to stoning for zina). The matn states that if the accused denies ihsan, it can be proven by the testimony of one man and two women, or by the fact that his wife gave birth to a child from him. The commentary explains that the birth of a child establishes marriage and entry, so it proves ihsan. The Hanafi position is that women's testimony is accepted for ihsan because it is not a pure hadd case; it is a condition that can be established by circumstantial evidence. The author refutes Zufar and al-Shafi'i: Zufar considers ihsan like a factor that aggravates the penalty, so he rejects women's testimony to avoid the hadd; al-Shafi'i rejects women's testimony in all non-financial matters. The Hanafi response is that ihsan is a set of beneficial conditions that prevent zina, not an aggravating cause, so women's testimony is accepted by analogy with other conditions. The commentary also includes a dispute among Hanafi imams about the wording of testimony for entry: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept 'dakhala biha' as sufficient, but Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani requires explicit mention of intercourse due to ambiguity. The passage ends with various sub-rulings about the effect of acknowledgments on ihsan and retraction of witnesses.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): The condition of being muhsan: free, adult, Muslim, in a valid marriage with consummation.
الرجوع (al-rujūʻ): Retraction of testimony by witnesses; here, if ihsan witnesses retract, they are not liable for diyah or other guarantee.
باضعها (bāḍaʻahā): A variant of 'jama'aha' (had intercourse with her).

Women's Testimony for Ihsan: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Zufar
Inter-madhhab dispute on women's testimony for ihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts the testimony of one man and two women to prove ihsan, and evaluate the counterarguments of al-Shafi'i and Zufar.

Core Idea
Ihsan is a praiseworthy quality, not an aggravating cause; thus women's testimony is accepted.

In hudud cases, establishing ihsan (being muhsan) is crucial for the punishment of stoning. But what happens when the accused denies ihsan? Can women's testimony be used? This lesson unpacks a key inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school accepts the testimony of one man and two women to prove ihsan, while al-Shafi'i and Zufar reject it. We'll explore the reasoning behind each position and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the core ruling: the Hanafi school holds that if a man denies ihsan, but a man and two women testify to his marriage, consummation, freedom, and Islam, then ihsan is proven and he is stoned. Also, if his wife gives birth to his child before the zina, that alone establishes ihsan.
The birth of a child is circumstantial evidence of intercourse, which suffices for ihsan.
2
Identify the Opponents and Their Views
Imam al-Shafi'i rejects women's testimony in non-financial matters altogether. Imam Zufar (a student of Abu Hanifa who later differed) argues that ihsan is like an effective cause ('illa) that aggravates the punishment, so women's testimony is not accepted as a precaution to avoid (dar') the hadd.
Zufar's analogy: if two dhimmis testify against a dhimmi that he freed his slave before zina, it is not accepted; similarly here.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
Al-Shafi'i's principle: women's testimony is only accepted in financial matters. Zufar's qiyas: ihsan is a condition that intensifies the punishment, so it resembles an effective cause; therefore, the strictest rules apply to avoid punishment.
Zufar's argument is based on the idea that the punishment is aggravated, so evidence should be more stringent.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response is that ihsan is not an effective cause but a set of praiseworthy qualities that prevent zina. It is a precondition, not a factor that aggravates the offense. Therefore, the same rules of testimony apply as in other matters where women's testimony is accepted (e.g., financial transactions). Also, ihsan can be established by circumstantial evidence like childbirth, which is not the case for actual punishments.
The text also argues that ihsan is not like retracting a confession, where women's testimony would be rejected.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: In a case where the accused denies ihsan and only a man and two women testify (with no man besides them), the Hanafi school would accept the testimony and stone the offender. The Shafi'i school would reject it, and the offender would receive the lighter punishment (100 lashes) instead of stoning.
This difference only arises when the defendant denies ihsan; if he confesses to being muhsan, the issue does not arise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Their testimony is accepted. And if he denies being muhsan, and a man and two women testify against him, or his wife gives birth from him, he is stoned. He is stoned. He said: (And if he denies ihsan and a man and two women testify against him, or his wife gives birth from him, he is stoned) meaning if he denies intercourse after the existence of all other conditions. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe that explains the ruling on establishing ihsan for stoning when the accused denies being muhsan. The author first states that the testimony of a man and two women is accepted, or if the wife gives birth, that also establishes ihsan. The commentary clarifies that 'or his wife gives birth' is understood as her having a child from him before the zina, because establishing lineage from him implies intercourse, which is a condition for ihsan. The main discussion is a dispute with Zufar and al-Shafi'i. Al-Shafi'i rejects women's testimony in non-financial matters. Zufar argues that ihsan is like an effective cause ('illa) that aggravates the punishment, so women's testimony should not be accepted to avoid (dar') the hadd. The Hanafi response, based on the commentary, is that ihsan is actually a set of praiseworthy qualities that prevent zina, not an aggravating factor; it is a precondition, not a cause. Therefore, women's testimony is accepted here just as it is in other contexts. The passage also distinguishes ihsan from punishments, which cannot be established by circumstantial evidence, unlike ihsan which can be proven by such evidence as the birth of a child.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsān): The state of being muhsan, i.e., a free adult Muslim who has engaged in valid marital intercourse. It is a condition for the punishment of stoning (rajm) for zina.

Manner of Testifying to Dukhul for Ihsan
Details the required wording for witnesses to prove dukhul (intercourse) for establishing ihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sufficient wording for testimony of intercourse to establish ihsan, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The phrase 'dakhala biha' suffices to prove intercourse for ihsan according to the Sahibayn; Imam Muhammad requires explicit wording.

In the Hanafi school, establishing ihsan (the state requiring stoning for zina) requires proof of actual intercourse. The wording used by witnesses matters. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a dispute among the Hanafi imams: the Sahibayn accept 'dakhala biha' as clear, while Imam Muhammad demands more explicit terms. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of Hanafi proof rules and the importance of linguistic precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal effect of ihsan
Ihsan makes a married person liable for stoning if they commit zina. It requires proof of consummation. The testimony must use appropriate wording.
2
Locate the disputed wording
The witnesses may say 'he entered with her' (dakhala biha) or use explicit terms like 'had intercourse' (jama'a) or 'penetrated' (bada'a). The dispute is whether 'dakhala biha' is sufficient.
3
Analyze the proofs
The Sahibayn argue that 'bi' (with) specifies intercourse when attached to a woman. Imam Muhammad argues that 'dakhala biha' is ambiguous, shared between intercourse, wedding procession, seclusion, and visiting.
Compare with 'dakhala 'alayha' which clearly means visiting.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn: 'dakhala biha' is sufficient. This is the position for fatwa.
This is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: وكيفية الشهادة بالدخول أن يقول الشهود تزوج امرأة وجامعها أو باضعها، ولو قالوا دخل بها يكفي عندهما. وقال محمد : لا يكفي ولا يثبت بذلك إحصانه لأنه مشترك بين الوطء والزفاف والخلوة والزيارة فلا يثبت بالشك كلفظ القربان والإتيان . ولهما أنه متى أضيف إلى المرأة بحرف الباء يتعين للجماع بخلاف دخل عليها فإنه للزيارة. ولو خلا بها ثم طلقها وقال وطئتها وأنكرت صار محصناً ،دونها، وكذا لو قالت بعد الطلاق كنت نصرانية وقال كانت مسلمة. وإذا كان أحد الزانيين محصناً يحد كل واحد منهما حده، وإن رجع شهود الإحصان لا يضمنون وهي معروفة. وفي المحيط : امرأة الرجل إذا أقرت أنها أمه هذا الرجل فزني الرجل يرجم، وإن أقرت بالرق قبل أن يدخل بها ثم زنى الرجل لا يرجم استحساناً لا قياساً رجل تزوج امرأة بغير ولي فدخل بها قال أبو يوسف: لا يكونان بذلك محصنين لأن هذا النكاح غير قطعاً لاختلاف العلماء والإخبار فيه اهـ. والله أعلم. صحيح بقولي: ولا تنظر لعورة أجنبي. بلا عذر كقابلة طبيب وختان وخافضة وحقن شهود زنا بلا قصد مريب وعلم بكارة في عنة أو زنا أو حين . رد للمعيب.
They said: The manner of testifying to intercourse is that the witnesses say: He married a woman and had intercourse with her, or he penetrated her. And if they said 'he entered with her' (dakhala biha), it is sufficient according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: It is not sufficient, and his ihsan is not established by that because it is shared between intercourse, wedding procession, seclusion, and visiting, so it is not established by doubt like the expressions qurban and itiyan. And for them (the two): When it is added to the woman with the letter ba', it is specific to intercourse, unlike 'dakhala 'alayha' which is for visiting. And if he secluded with her then divorced her and said 'I had intercourse with her' and she denied it, he becomes muhsan, but not her. Likewise if she said after divorce 'I was a Christian' and he said 'she was Muslim'. And if one of the two fornicators is muhsan, each is punished with his own punishment (i.e., the muhsan is stoned, the non-muhsan is lashed). And if the witnesses to ihsan retract, they do not guarantee (anything), and that is known. And in al-Muhit: If a man's wife confesses that she is the mother of this man, then the man commits zina, he is stoned. And if she confesses to being a slave before he had intercourse with her, then the man commits zina, he is not stoned by istihsan, not by qiyas. A man married a woman without a guardian and had intercourse with her – Abu Yusuf said: Neither becomes muhsan by that, because this marriage is definitively invalid due to the disagreement of scholars and reports. Allah knows best. Correct with my statement: And do not look at the private parts of a non-mahram. Without excuse like midwife, doctor, circumciser, cupper, injection, witnesses of zina without suspicious intent, and knowledge of virginity in impotence or zina or at the time. Return for defect.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rules on the wording of testimony for dukhul (intercourse) to establish ihsan. The author explains that witnesses should explicitly say 'he married and had intercourse' or 'he penetrated'. There is a dispute among the Hanafi imams: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani accept the phrase 'dakhala biha' (entered with her) as sufficient because the preposition 'bi' specifies intercourse, whereas Imam Muhammad alone requires more explicit wording because 'dakhala biha' could be ambiguous. The text then gives a case: if a man secludes with his wife, divorces her, and claims he had intercourse but she denies, he becomes muhsan (since his claim is credible against himself) but she does not. Another case: if the wife confesses after divorce that she was a Christian, but the husband says she was Muslim, the ruling depends. If one of the two fornicators is muhsan, each receives their respective hadd. Retraction of witnesses to ihsan does not subject them to liability (they don't pay diya or face retaliation). The passage ends with a note from al-Muhit about cases where the wife's confession affects the husband's ihsan status, and a case of marriage without a guardian where Abu Yusuf rules that such a marriage is void (batil) due to ikhtilaf, so it does not establish ihsan. The final sentence appears to be a separate note about looking at private parts in medical contexts.

Key Terms
دخل بها (dakhala bihā): A phrase meaning 'he entered with her' which, according to the Sahibayn, is sufficient to establish intercourse for ihsan, as the preposition 'bi' (with) specifies the meaning of sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which phrase is sufficient to prove dukhul (intercourse) for establishing ihsan?
A) 'Dakhala 'alayha' (he entered upon her)
B) 'Dakhala biha' (he entered with her)
C) 'Khalā bihā' (he secluded with her)
D) 'Tazawwaja bihā' (he married her)

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'dakhala biha' is sufficient to prove intercourse for ihsan according to the majority Hanafi view (Sahibayn), while Imam Muhammad's stricter requirement is not the relied-upon position.

Introduction to Hadd for Drinking: Conditions and Proof
Opens the chapter on hadd for drinking, stating the ruling, conditions, and the relevant hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for establishing the hadd for drinking according to the Hanafi school and explain the derivation from the hadith.

Core Idea
The hadd for drinking requires the smell of wine or intoxication, established by two male witnesses or confession.

The hadd for drinking is a fixed punishment that must be implemented by the state. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the prerequisites: the presence of the smell of wine or visible intoxication, and the requirement of two male witnesses or a confession. The proof is a hadith commanding flogging, with the fourth-instance killing abrogated. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying this punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is drinking wine or any intoxicant (nabidh). The ruling is the hadd: flogging (80 lashes for free, 40 for slave, though number not detailed here).
The hadd is a fixed punishment, not discretionary.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever drinks wine, flog him...' from the four Sunan except al-Nasa'i. The killing in the fourth instance is abrogated by the practice narrated by al-Nasa'i.
This is a Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the ruling is qati' al-dalala due to clear imperative.
3
Analyze the conditions for evidence
Two conditions for proof: 1) The accused is taken with the smell of wine present, or is intoxicated. 2) Testimony of two male witnesses or one confession. The smell must be present at the time of testimony or at the time of bringing the accused, depending on proximity.
Women's testimony is not accepted in hudud due to shubha.
4
Understand the details of smell requirement
If the place is near, the smell must be present when giving testimony (or the judge may order smelling). If the place is distant and smell faded, witnesses must explicitly state they took him while smell was present.
The author prefers to link the smell condition directly to the drink, as in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد الشرب من شرب خمراً وأخذ وريحها موجود أو كان سكران ولو بنبيذ وشهد رجلان أو أقر مرة حدان علم شربه طوعاً وصحاً للحديث «من شرب الخمر فاجلدوه ثم إن شرب فاجلدوه ثم إن شرب فاجلدوه فإن عاد في الرابعة فاقتلوه»(1) أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة إلا النسائي. ثم نسخ القتل في الرابعة بما رواه النسائي أنه عليه السلام قد أتى برجل شرب الخمر في الرابعة فجلدوه ولم يقتله. وزاد في لفظ فرأى المسلمون أن الحد قد وقع وأن القتل قد ارتفع أطلق في شرب الخمر فشمل القطرة الواحدة كما سیصرح به به آخراً، وفي وجود ريحها فشمل ما إذا كان الريح موجوداً وقت الشهادة أو وقت رفعه إلى الحاكم وهي على وجهين فإن كان المكان قريباً فلا بد من وجود الرائحة عند أداء الشهادة بأن يشهدا بالشرب وبقيام الرائحة أو يشهدا به فقط فيأمر القاضي باستنكاهه فيستنكهه ويخبره بأن ريحها موجود، فإن شهدا به بعد مضي ريحها مع قرب المكان فسيأتي، وإن كان المكان بعيداً فزالت الرائحة فلا بد أن يشهدا بالشرب ويقولا أخذناه وريحها موجود لأن مجيئهم به من مكان بعيد لا يستلزم كونهم أخذوه في حال قيام الرائحة فيحتاجون إلى ذكر ذلك للحاكم . ولو أخر المصنف اشتراط وجود الرائحة عن السكران بأن قال بعد قوله «ولو بنبيذ» «وأخذ وريح ما شرب منه موجود لكان أولى لأنه لا بد من وجود رائحة الشرب الذي شربه خمراً كان أو نبيذاً سكر منه . وقد ذكر المصنف الريح حيث قال «موجود». وفي الهداية وريحها موجودة وهو الحق لأن الريح من الأسماء المؤنثة السماعية كما في غاية البيان. وقيد بالرجلين لأن شهادة النساء لا تقبل في الحدود للشبهة. ولم يذكر المصنف أن القاضي يسأل الشهود كما يسألهم في الزنا وقد ذكره قاضيخان في الفتاوى فقال : وإذا شهد
Chapter on Hadd for Drinking. Whoever drinks wine and is taken while its smell is present, or was intoxicated even by nabidh (date-wine), and two men testify or he confesses once, he is punished with the hadd, provided he drank voluntarily and the drinking is confirmed. Due to the hadith: 'Whoever drinks wine, flog him; then if he drinks, flog him; then if he drinks, flog him; then if he returns a fourth time, kill him.' It was narrated by the authors of the four Sunan except al-Nasa'i. Then the killing in the fourth instance was abrogated by what al-Nasa'i narrated: that he (peace be upon him) was brought a man who drank wine a fourth time, so they flogged him and did not kill him. And in another wording: 'So the Muslims saw that the hadd had been established and that the killing was removed.' He used the absolute term 'drinking wine' which includes even a single drop, as will be clarified later. And in the presence of its smell, it includes whether the smell is present at the time of testimony or at the time of bringing him to the judge, and this has two aspects. If the place is near, then the presence of the smell is necessary at the time of giving testimony: either they testify to the drinking and the persistence of the smell, or they testify only to the drinking and the judge orders that his mouth be smelled, so he smells it and informs him that its smell is present. If they testify after the smell has dissipated even though the place is near, then it will come later. And if the place is distant and the smell has dissipated, then they must testify to the drinking and say: we took him while its smell was present, because bringing him from a distant place does not necessitate that they took him while the smell was present; so they need to mention that to the judge. And if the author had delayed the requirement of the presence of smell after the mention of the intoxicated person, such that after saying 'even by nabidh' he said 'and he is taken while the smell of what he drank is present', it would have been more appropriate, because the smell of the drink he drank, whether wine or nabidh from which he became intoxicated, must be present. And the author mentioned the smell where he said 'present'. And in al-Hidayah: 'and its smell is present' – this is correct because 'rih' is among the feminine nouns that are samā'ī (based on linguistic usage) as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is restricted to two men because the testimony of women is not accepted in hadd punishments due to doubt. And the author did not mention that the judge questions the witnesses as he questions them in zina, but Qadikhan mentioned it in al-Fatawa, saying: 'When they testify...'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the hadd punishment for drinking. The ruling is that whoever drinks wine (or any intoxicating beverage like nabidh) and is caught either with the smell of wine on his breath or in a state of intoxication, and two male witnesses testify or he confesses once, receives the hadd. The proof is the famous hadith instructing flogging for drinking, with the fourth-time penalty of death being abrogated. The commentary explains that the hadd applies even for a single drop. A key condition is the presence of the smell of wine at the time of testimony or at the time the case is brought before the judge. The text distinguishes between near and distant places regarding the requirement of smell. The author of the sharh (Ibn Nujaym) notes that it would have been better for the matn author to explicitly link the smell requirement to the drink itself. The Hidayah uses the feminine form 'rijuhā' for smell, which is correct linguistically. Women's testimony is not accepted in hadd punishments due to the principle of avoiding punishment in cases of doubt (shubha). Finally, the judge is supposed to question the witnesses, as recorded by Qadikhan.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (hadd al-shurb): The fixed corporal punishment for drinking intoxicants. It is established by the testimony of two men or confession, and requires evidence of intoxication or smell of wine.
ريح (rīḥ): The smell of wine, a crucial piece of circumstantial evidence for establishing the hadd for drinking. Its presence at the time of witnessing or at the time of bringing the accused is necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what suffices to prove that a person consumed wine for the purpose of imposing the hadd of drinking?
A) Only the person's confession is needed.
B) The smell of wine on the breath or visible intoxication, with two male witnesses or confession.
C) Only if the person is caught in the act of drinking.
D) The presence of wine at the scene.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking is established by the smell of wine or intoxication, proven by two male witnesses or confession, and the hadith commands flogging with abrogation of killing.
