Definition and Proof of Hadd al-Qadhf
Defines hadd al-qadhf with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition, punishment, and proof of hadd al-qadhf, and identify the conditions for its application.

Core Idea
Accusing a chaste person of zina incurs 80 lashes — a fixed hadd proven by Qur'an and Ijma.

This passage opens the chapter on hadd al-qadhf. It defines the crime as accusing a muhsan (chaste) person of zina, with the punishment fixed at 80 lashes for a free person and 40 for a slave. The proof is from the Qur'anic verse (An-Nur:4) and consensus. The text also clarifies that only accusations of zina trigger hadd; other accusations lead to ta'zir.

Guided Path
1
Define qadhf and identify its essential elements
Find the definition in the text: 'accusing a muhsan of zina'. Note that the victim must be muhsan and the accusation must be zina.
The term 'muhsan' means chaste, here specifically not known for fornication.
2
Identify the punishment quantity and its basis
The text states 80 lashes for a free person and half for a slave, likened to the hadd for drinking. Note the analogy (qiyas) used.
This is the Hanafi position; other schools may differ on the slave's hadd.
3
Recognize the primary proof: Quran and Ijma
The author cites Surah An-Nur:4 as the Qur'anic proof and mentions that hadd is established by Ijma (consensus). Understand the imperative 'فاجلدوهم' as indicating obligation.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah according to Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the procedural proof requirements
The text explains that qadhf is proven by two male witnesses or the confession of the qadhif (accuser) once. Women's testimony, testimony upon testimony, and a judge's letter are not accepted.
This mirrors the strict evidentiary rules for zina itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب حد القذف
فاجلدوهم :
حد القذف
تأباه لأن العلة فيه لحوق العار وهو مفقود في الخلوة. وينبغي أن يقيد أيضاً بكون المقذوف محصناً كما قيد به في الآية الكريمة فقذف غير المحصن لا يكون من الكبائر ولذا لم يجب به الحد فينبغي أن : يعرف القذف في الشرع بأنه المحصن بالزنا. وفي فتح القدير : وتعلق رمي الحد به بالإجماع مستندين إلى قوله تعالى والذين يرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتوا بأربعة شهداء ثمانين جلدة [النور: ٤] والمراد الرمي بالزنا حتى لو رماها بسائر المعاصي غيره لا يجب الحد بل التعزير، وفي النص إشارة إليه أي إلى أن المراد بالزنا وهو اشتراط أربعة من الشهود يشهدون عليها بما رماها به ليظهر به صدقه فيما رماها به ولا شيء يتوقف ثبوته بالشهادة على شهادة أربعة إلا الزنا ثم ثبت وجوب جلد القاذف للمحصن بدلالة هذا النص للقطع بإلغاء الفارق وهو صفة الأنوثة واستقلال دفع عار ما نسب إليه بالتأثير بحيث لا يتوقف فهمه على ثبوت أهلية الاجتهاد . قوله : (هو) كحد الشرب كمية وثبوتاً) أي كحد الشرب قدراً وهو ثمانون سوطاً إن كان حراً ونصفه إن كان القاذف عبداً، ويثبت سببه وهو القذف بشهادة رجلين أو بإقرار القاذف مرة ولا تقبل فيه شهادة النساء ولا الشهادة على الشهادة ولا كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي.
The Book of Hudud: Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. So flog them: The hadd of qadhf. It is disliked because the cause in it is disgrace, and it is absent in seclusion. And it should also be restricted by the condition that the victim is muhsan, as it is restricted in the noble verse. So qadhf of a non-muhsan is not from the major sins, and therefore hadd is not obligatory due to it. So it is appropriate to define qadhf in Shari'ah as accusing a muhsan of zina. And in Fath al-Qadir: The obligation of hadd for it is established by consensus, relying on His statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes' [An-Nur:4]. And what is meant is accusation of zina, such that if he accuses her of other sins, hadd is not obligatory but ta'zir. And in the text is an indication that what is meant is zina, which is the requirement of four witnesses who testify concerning what he accused her of, so that his truthfulness in his accusation appears. And nothing is established by testimony on the testimony of four except zina. Then the obligation of flogging the qadhif for a muhsan is established by the indication of this text, due to the certainty of eliminating the difference (between male and female), and the independence of repelling the disgrace attributed to him by effect, such that its understanding does not depend on establishing the capability of ijtihad. His statement: 'It is like the hadd of drinking in quantity and establishment' means in amount: eighty lashes if free and half if the qadhif is a slave. And its cause is established, which is qadhf, by the testimony of two men or by the confession of the qadhif once, and the testimony of women is not accepted in it, nor testimony upon testimony, nor the letter of a judge to a judge.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on hadd al-qadhf. It first states that the hadd is 80 lashes for a free person and half for a slave, drawing an analogy with the hadd for drinking. It then presents the Quranic basis from Surah An-Nur:4, noting that the verse specifies 'muhsanat' (chaste women), so the victim must be muhsan. The passage clarifies that only accusations of zina trigger hadd; other accusations result in ta'zir. It also explains that the proof for hadd is by two male witnesses or one confession, and women's testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A free adult Muslim who is chaste (not known for fornication).
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for a specific offense.
القذف (al-qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the required number of lashes for a free person convicted of qadhf?
A) 40
B) 80
C) 100
D) 20

Key Takeaway
The hadd for qadhf is 80 lashes for a free person, based on Quran (An-Nur:4) and Ijma, and applies only when a muhsan person is accused of zina, proven by two male witnesses or confession.

Qadhf in Seclusion: Is It a Major Sin?
Discussion on whether qadhf in seclusion is a major sin requiring hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qadhf in seclusion is a major sin and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Qadhf in seclusion is a major sin because the audacity against Allah outweighs the absence of public harm.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a nuanced ikhtilaf: whether accusing a chaste person of zina in complete privacy constitutes a major sin. The Hanafi school, as presented by al-Haskafi, argues that it does, while some Shafi'i scholars disagree. Let's trace the proofs and refine our understanding of the conditions for hadd and kabirah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding qadhf in seclusion: it is a major sin (kabirah) even if hadd is not applied.
Al-Haskafi's view is the mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i scholar Ibn Abd al-Salam claims it is not a major sin because the harm (disgrace) is absent in seclusion.
Some later Shafi'is like al-Ghazzi eventually agreed it is a major sin.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the reasoning: since no one hears, the victim is not dishonored, so the hadd is not obligatory, and hence it is not a major sin.
Al-Luqani and al-Zarkashi refine this by distinguishing negation of hadd from negation of sin.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the condition of muhsan is for hadd alone; the sin stems from the audacity against Allah, which remains even if truthful and in private.
The hadith from al-Tabarani about qadhf of a dhimmi supports that it is a major sin deserving punishment in the afterlife.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the Shafi'i view, the act is not a major sin; according to the Hanafi view, it is a major sin liable for ta'zir even if hadd is not applied.
This affects the mufti's fatwa on the gravity of the sin and the appropriate punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكره عبارة المؤلف أقول : المذكور في جمع الجوامع للمحلى . قال ابن عبد السلام : قذف المحصن في الخلوة بحيث لا يسمعه الله تعالى والحفظة ليس بكبيرة موجبة للحد لانتفاء المفسدة. وقال محشيه اللقاني : المحقق من مثل هذه العبارة نفي إيجاب الحد لا نفي كونه كبيرة أيضاً لأن الكلام المقيد بقيود إذا نفي توجه النفي للقيد الأخير ويصير الكلام صادقاً بنفي غيره وبثبوته .اهـ. وقال الزركشي قال ابن عبد السلام : الظاهر أن من قذف محصناً في خلوته ليس بكبيرة موجبة للحد لانتفاء المفسدة. وما قاله قد يظهر فيما إذا كان صادقاً دون الكاذب لجراءته على الله تعالى اهـ فتأمل اهـ. وفي شرح الملتقى للحصكفي قلت : والذي حررته في شرح منظومة والد شيخنا تبعاً لشيخنا النجم الغزي الشافعي من الكبائر وإن كان صادقاً ولا شهود له عليه ولو من الوالد لولده أو لولد ولده وإن لم يحد به بل يعزر ولو لغير محصن وشرط الفقهاء الإحصان إنما هو لوجوب الحد لا لكونه كبيرة وقد روى الطبراني عن واثلة عن النبي الله أنه قال من قذف ذمياً حد له يوم القيمة بسياط من نار»
He mentioned the author's statement: I say: Mentioned in Jami' al-Jawami' by al-Mahalli. Ibn Abd al-Salam said: Qadhf of a muhsan in seclusion such that no one but Allah and the angels hears it is not a major sin that entails hadd because the harm (disgrace) is absent. His commentator al-Luqani said: The verified meaning from such an expression is the negation of the obligation of hadd, not the negation of it being a major sin, because speech restricted by conditions, when negated, the negation is directed to the last restriction, and the speech becomes true by negating others and by their affirmation. And al-Zarkashi said: Ibn Abd al-Salam said: The apparent is that whoever qadhfs a muhsan in seclusion is not committing a major sin that entails hadd because the harm is absent. What he said may appear in the case where he is truthful, not the liar, due to his audacity against Allah. So reflect. And in Sharh al-Multaqa by al-Haskafi: I said: What I have verified in Sharh al-Manzuma of my father's teacher, following our teacher Najm al-Ghazzi al-Shafi'i, is that it is from the major sins even if truthful and even if he has no witnesses against him, even from a father to his son or grandson, even if he is not flogged for it, but rather is given ta'zir, even for a non-muhsan. And the condition of ihsan by the jurists is only for the obligation of hadd, not for it being a major sin. And al-Tabarani narrated from Wathila from the Prophet (SAW) that he said: 'Whoever qadhfs a dhimmi will have a hadd for him on the Day of Resurrection with whips of fire.'
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific issue: if someone accuses a chaste person of zina in complete seclusion, does the hadd punishment apply? Ibn Abd al-Salam (Shafi'i) argues it does not, and is not even a major sin because no one heard, so the victim is not dishonored. Al-Luqani refines this, saying only the hadd is negated, not the sinfulness. Al-Zarkashi adds that if the accuser is truthful but cannot produce witnesses, it may still be a major sin due to audacity against Allah. Al-Haskafi, following the Shafi'i al-Ghazzi, states it remains a major sin even if truthful, and the condition of muhsan is only for hadd, not for the sin. He supports this with a hadith about qadhf of a dhimmi.

Key Terms
كبيرة (kabirah): Major sin, one of the grave offenses.
خلوة (khalwah): Seclusion, privacy where no one else is present.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment less than hadd, determined by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented by al-Haskafi, is qadhf in seclusion a major sin?
A) No, because no one heard
B) Yes, even if no one heard
C) Only if the accuser is lying
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
Qadhf in seclusion is a major sin because the rebellion against Allah's command makes it grave, regardless of public knowledge or application of hadd.

Imprisonment of the Accused in Qadhf Cases
Rulings on imprisonment of the accused and examination of witnesses in qadhf cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on imprisoning the qadhf accused based on one witness and apply the distance condition.

Core Idea
One upright witness plus a second in the city triggers imprisonment according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to Abu Yusuf.

This lesson focuses on a procedural matter in hudud: may the qadi imprison the accused before trial? The ruling hinges on the availability of witnesses and their distance from the court. The source presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa permits imprisonment if one upright witness is present and another is in the city, while Abu Yusuf disagrees. Additionally, a three-day travel distance condition is discussed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for imprisonment
The passage states that if the plaintiff brings one upright witness and claims another is in the city, the qadi imprisons him according to Abu Hanifa. Note that the witness must be upright (adl).
The condition is one upright witness + claim of a second in the city.
2
Examine the distance rule
The text adds a qualification: this applies if the location of the second witness is far (beyond three days travel); if close (within three days), the accused is also imprisoned? Actually, the text says 'he also imprisons him' for close distance, meaning imprisonment is allowed in both cases. So distance does not affect permissibility.
The distance rule is mentioned but does not change the ruling.
3
State the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa allows imprisonment with one witness; Abu Yusuf does not. The passage does not state the reason for the disagreement, but it likely stems from different views on the sufficiency of evidence for pretrial detention.
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are in agreement against Abu Hanifa on this point.
4
Understand the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if the qadi follows Abu Hanifa, he will detain the accused; if he follows Abu Yusuf, he will release him pending trial. This affects the accused's liberty before a hadd proceeding.
No mufta bihi is given, so the opinion followed depends on the qadi's school practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحبسه؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي الظهيرية هذا إذا كان المكان الذي فيه الشاهد بعيداً من المصر بحيث لا يمكنه الإحضار في ثلاثة أيام، أما إذا كان المكان قريباً يمكنه الإحضار في ثلاثة أيام فإنه يحبسه أيضاً. وفي الظهيرية أيضاً : إذا ادعى رجل على رجل أنه قذفه وجاء بشاهدين فالقاضي يسأل الشاهدين عن القذف ما هو وكيف هو، فإذا قالا نشهد أنه قال له يا زاني قبلت شهادتهما وحد القاذف إن كانا عدلين فإن شهد أحدهما أنه قال له يا زاني يوم وشهد الآخر أنه قال له يا زاني يوم الخميس قال أبو حنيفة : تقبل هذه الشهادة. وقالا : لا تقبل، وكذا لو شهد أحدهما بالإقرار والآخر بالإنشاء اهـ.
He imprisons him; thus in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Zahiriya: This is when the location of the witness is far from the city such that he cannot bring him within three days; if the location is close enough to bring him within three days, he also imprisons him. And in al-Zahiriya also: If a man claims that another man qadhfed him and brings two witnesses, the qadi asks the witnesses about the qadhf: what it is and how it is. If they say: We testify that he said to him 'O fornicator!' their testimony is accepted and the qadhif is flogged if they are upright. If one testifies that he said it on a certain day and the other testifies that he said it on Thursday, Abu Hanifa said: this testimony is accepted. They both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not accepted. Similarly, if one testifies to confession and the other to direct accusation, it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage deals with procedural rules. If the plaintiff claims to have witnesses, the qadi may imprison the accused. Abu Hanifa's view is that imprisonment is allowed even if only one upright witness is present and the other is in the city. Abu Yusuf disagrees. The distance condition (three days travel) determines whether the defendant is released. The qadi must question witnesses about the specific words used in the qadhf. If witnesses differ on the day, Abu Hanifa accepts the testimony, but the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require agreement on the time. Similarly, if one witness testifies that the defendant confessed to qadhf and the other testifies to the direct qadhf, it is not accepted.

Key Terms
بينة حاضرة (bayyinah hadirah): Witnesses present in the city.
حبس (habs): Imprisonment by the qadi pending proceedings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for the qadi to imprison the accused based on Abu Hanifa's view?
A) The plaintiff must bring two upright witnesses.
B) The plaintiff must bring one upright witness and claim a second is in the city.
C) The accused must confess.
D) The plaintiff must provide a surety.

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment in qadhf cases is not automatic; it hinges on the presence of one upright witness plus a claim of a second, and even then there is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Accepting Testimony When Witnesses Differ on Time or Type
Rulings on imprisonment of the accused and examination of witnesses in qadhf cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when testimony in qadhf is accepted according to Abu Hanifa and when it is rejected by the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to similar discrepancies.

Core Idea
If witnesses disagree on the day of qadhf, Abu Hanifa accepts their testimony; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad reject it.

This lesson examines the second part of the passage, which addresses evidentiary issues in qadhf: what happens when two witnesses differ on the specific day of the offense, or when one testifies to confession and the other to direct accusation? The ruling is clear that testimony on confession vs direct accusation is always rejected, but there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the day discrepancy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a situation where the plaintiff brings two witnesses to a qadhf. The qadi first asks them about the act of qadhf: what was said and how. If they both testify to the same words (e.g., 'You are a fornicator'), the testimony is accepted and the hadd is imposed if they are upright.
This is the baseline: agreement on the substance of the qadhf.
2
Note the first discrepancy: differing days
If one witness testifies that the defendant said the qadhf on a certain day (e.g., 'on a day') and the other says 'on Thursday,' there is a disagreement. Abu Hanifa accepts this testimony; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not.
The disagreement is over whether the day is an essential part of the testimony or a minor detail.
3
Note the second discrepancy: confession vs direct accusation
If one witness testifies that the defendant confessed to qadhf (إقرار) and the other testifies to the direct qadhf (إنشاء), the testimony is not accepted. This is not disputed; the passage says 'وكذا' (similarly).
This is a separate ruling: the two testimonies are inconsistent in nature and thus not accepted.
4
State the Hanafi positions
For the day discrepancy: Abu Hanifa accepts, Sahibayn reject. For confession vs direct: all agree it is not accepted.
The thamarah: if the qadi follows Abu Hanifa, the hadd is imposed; if he follows the Sahibayn, the case is dismissed for lack of consistent testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحبسه؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي الظهيرية هذا إذا كان المكان الذي فيه الشاهد بعيداً من المصر بحيث لا يمكنه الإحضار في ثلاثة أيام، أما إذا كان المكان قريباً يمكنه الإحضار في ثلاثة أيام فإنه يحبسه أيضاً. وفي الظهيرية أيضاً : إذا ادعى رجل على رجل أنه قذفه وجاء بشاهدين فالقاضي يسأل الشاهدين عن القذف ما هو وكيف هو، فإذا قالا نشهد أنه قال له يا زاني قبلت شهادتهما وحد القاذف إن كانا عدلين فإن شهد أحدهما أنه قال له يا زاني يوم وشهد الآخر أنه قال له يا زاني يوم الخميس قال أبو حنيفة : تقبل هذه الشهادة. وقالا : لا تقبل، وكذا لو شهد أحدهما بالإقرار والآخر بالإنشاء اهـ.
He imprisons him; thus in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Zahiriya: This is when the location of the witness is far from the city such that he cannot bring him within three days; if the location is close enough to bring him within three days, he also imprisons him. If one testifies that he said it on a certain day and the other testifies that he said it on Thursday, Abu Hanifa said: this testimony is accepted. Abu Hanifa's view is that imprisonment is allowed even if only one upright witness is present and the other is in the city. Abu Yusuf disagrees. The distance condition (three days travel) determines whether the defendant is released. The qadi must question witnesses about the specific words used in the qadhf. If witnesses differ on the day, Abu Hanifa accepts the testimony, but the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require agreement on the time. Key Terms

حبس (habs): Imprisonment by the qadi pending proceedings.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession to the qadhf.
إنشاء (insha'): Direct accusation of qadhf.

Key Takeaway

Conditions for Hadd al-Qadhf: Muhsan, Demand, and Explicit Wording
Explains conditions for hadd: victim must be muhsan, request, and exact wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for applying hadd al-qadhf in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the phrase 'أنت أزنى'.

Core Idea
Hadd al-qadhf requires the victim to be muhsan, to demand punishment, and the accusation to be of zina in explicit terms.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines the essential conditions for the fixed punishment (hadd) for false accusation of zina (qadhf). Understanding these conditions is crucial because the hadd is a severe penalty and is only applied when strict requirements are met. The text also highlights a key intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether phrases like 'you are more adulterous' constitute qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qadhf (accusing a muhsan of zina). The ruling is that the accuser is subject to hadd (80 lashes) if the victim demands it and the accuser cannot produce four witnesses.
The hadd is wajib upon fulfillment of conditions.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is Quran 24:4, which mentions 'those who accuse chaste women (muhsanat) and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes.'
The verse explicitly ties the punishment to the victim being muhsan and the accuser's inability to prove the accusation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse implies three conditions: the victim must be muhsan, the accusation must be of zina (since 'رمى' in the context of zina), and the punishment is only applied when the accuser fails to produce witnesses. The text also notes that the victim's demand is required, derived from the verse's implication of a right of the victim.
The condition of demand is supported by consensus, as mentioned in the text.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether phrases like 'أنت أزنى الناس' (you are the most adulterous of people) or 'أنت أزنى من فلان' (you are more adulterous than so-and-so) constitute qadhf. Some Hanafi works (al-Mabsut, al-Khaniyya) say no hadd because these phrases imply capability, not an actual accusation. Others (Qadikhan, al-Zahiriyya) say hadd is wajib.
The text quotes al-Mabsut: 'معناه أنت أقدر الناس على الزنا' (it means you are the most capable of zina).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether the qadi imposes hadd or not. The text does not give a clear tarjih but mentions the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that there is no hadd for such phrases. This suggests the preferred view may be no hadd, but the dispute remains.
The student should understand that such comparative phrases are not clear accusations and lead to disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو قذف محصناً أو محصنة بزنا حد بطلبه (مفرقاً أي بطلب المقذوف مفرقاً على أعضاء القاذف لما تلوناه من الآية وبينا من الإجماع قيد بالمحصن لأن غيره لا يجب الحد بقذفه، وفيه إشارة إلى اشتراط عجز القاذف عن إقامة البينة على الزنا فإنه إذا أقام بينة على صدق مقالته لم يبق المقذوف محصناً فأغنى ذكر الإحصان عن هذا الشرط، وكذا لو صدقه المقذوف، وفي الظهيرية : رجل قذف رجلاً بالزنا فرفعه المقذوف إلى القاضي فقال القاذف عندي شهود عدول على ما قلت وأقامهم على ذلك فإنه لا يحد. وهل يحد المقذوف؟ إن شهدوا بحد متقادم فإنه لا يحد كما لو شهدوا عليه بالزنا قبل القذف إن كان متقادماً لم يحد، وإن كان غير متقادم حد فكذلك ههنا .اهـ. وقيد بقوله «بزنا» لأنه لو قذفه بغيره لا يكون قذفاً شرعاً لما قدمناه فلا حد بقوله وطئك فلان وطئاً حراماً أو جامعك حراماً. وأطلق في الزنا ولم يقيده بلفظ ليدخل فيه ما إذا قال زنيت أو يا زاني أو أنت أزنى الناس أو أنت أزنى من فلان أو أنت أزنى مني كما في الظهيرية، ويخالفه ما في الخانية : لو قال أنت أزنى . لا حد مني (فالقاضي يسأل الشاهدين عن القذف الخ) قال الحموي : وينبغي أن يسألهما عن المكان لاحتمال أن يكون قذفه في دار الحرب أو البغي وعن الزمان لاحتمال أن يكون قذفه في صباه لا لاحتمال التقادم لأنه لا يبطل به بخلاف سائر الحدود ثم رأيت الأول في البدائع. اهـ. أبو السعود. قوله : (وكذا لو شهد أحدهما بالإقرار الخ قال أبو السعود يفيد قبول هذه الشهادة عند الإمام، وكلامه في النهر يفيد الاتفاق على أنها لا تقبل ونصه ولو شهد أحدهما أنه قذفه يوم الخميس والآخر أنه أقر بقذفه في ذلك اليوم لم يحد في قولهم قوله : (ويخالفه ما في الخانية (الخ كذا يخالفه ما في الجوهرة إذا قال أنت أزنى الناس فإنه لا يحد لأن معناه أنت أقدر الناس على الزنا .اهـ. والظاهر أن علة ما في الخانية هذه وعليه فيكون أنت أزنى من فلان الزاني أو من فلان مثل أزنى الناس وأزنى مني : تأمل . ثم رأيته في النهر قال : وفي أنت أزنى الناس أو من فلان خلاف ففي المبسوط لا حد عليه إذ معناه أنت أقدر الناس على الزنا، وجزم قاضيخان بوجوبه، وكذا في أنت أزنى مني فجزم في الظهيرية بوجوبه، وفي الخانية بأنه لا يجب اهـ. وأوضح المراد في التتارخانية حيث قال نقلاً عن المحيط : وفي كتاب الاختلاف روى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة إذا قال لغيره أنت أزنى الناس، أنت أزني من
His statement: 'So if he qadhfs a muhsan or muhsanah with zina, he is flogged at his request, distributed over the limbs of the qadhif.' Meaning: at the request of the victim, distributed over the limbs of the qadhif, based on the verse we recited and the consensus we mentioned. He restricted it with muhsan because no hadd is wajib by qadhf of a non-muhsan. It contains an indication of the condition that the qadhif is unable to bring evidence of zina; for if he brings evidence of the truth of his statement, the victim ceases to be muhsan. So mentioning muhsan suffices for this condition. Similarly, if the victim confirms him. In al-Zahiriyya: A man qadhfed a man with zina, and the victim brought it to the qadi, and the qadhif said: I have upright witnesses on what I said, and he brought them, then he is not flogged. And will the victim be flogged? If they testify to a hadd that is old (taqaddum), then he is not flogged, just as if they testify against him for zina before the qadhf if it was old, he is not flogged; if it was not old, he is flogged. So likewise here. And he restricted it with 'with zina' because if he qadhfs him with something else, it is not qadhf legally, as we have mentioned. So there is no hadd by his saying 'so-and-so had unlawful intercourse with you' or 'he had unlawful union with you'. And he left (the word) zina unrestricted, not specifying a particular expression, to include cases where he says 'you fornicated' or 'O fornicator' or 'you are the most adulterous of people' or 'you are more adulterous than so-and-so' or 'you are more adulterous than me', as in al-Zahiriyya. And it is contradicted by what is in al-Khaniyya: if he says 'you are more adulterous than me', no hadd. (The qadi asks the two witnesses about the qadhf etc.) Al-Hamawi said: He should ask them about the place, because it is possible that he qadhfed him in the land of war or rebellion, and about the time, because it is possible that he qadhfed him in his childhood, not because of the possibility of lapse of time (taqadum), because it does not invalidate it, contrary to other hudud. Then I saw the first in al-Bada'i. Abu al-Su'ud. His statement: 'Similarly, if one testifies to confession and the other to direct accusation.' Abu al-Su'ud said: It indicates acceptance of this testimony according to the Imam, and his statement in al-Nahr indicates agreement that it is not accepted. Its text: If one testifies that he qadhfed him on Thursday and the other that he confessed to qadhf on that day, hadd is not executed in their opinion. His statement: 'And it is contradicted by what is in al-Khaniyya' etc. So it is contradicted by what is in al-Jawhara: if he says 'you are the most adulterous of people', he is not flogged because its meaning is 'you are the most capable of zina'. And it appears that the cause of what is in al-Khaniyya is this, so therefore 'you are more adulterous than so-and-so the adulterer' or 'than so-and-so' like 'the most adulterous' and 'more adulterous than me': reflect. Then I saw in al-Nahr he said: In 'you are the most adulterous of people' or 'than so-and-so' there is a disagreement. In al-Mabsut, no hadd upon him, as its meaning is 'you are the most capable of zina'. Qadikhan decisively ruled its obligation. Similarly in 'you are more adulterous than me', al-Zahiriyya ruled its obligation, and al-Khaniyya that it is not wajib. And the intended meaning is clarified in al-Tatarkhaniyya where he said, quoting from al-Muhit: And in Kitab al-Ikhtilaf, Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he says to another 'you are the most adulterous of people', 'you are more adulterous than'.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage summarizes the key conditions for applying hadd al-qadhf. First, the victim must be muhsan (chaste). Second, the punishment is only carried out if the victim demands it (bitalabihi). Third, the accusation must be of zina specifically, using words like 'zani' or 'zana' or 'you are more adulterous than so-and-so'. There is a dispute about phrases like 'you are the most adulterous of people' – some say it implies capability, not accusation, so no hadd. The passage also addresses the scenario where the accused brings witnesses to prove the zina: if they testify to recent zina, the accusation is proven true and the victim may be flogged instead (if the victim is not muhsan). If they testify to old zina (mutalaqadam), then it is not accepted and the qadhif is flogged. The passage also discusses the need to ask witnesses about place and time to avoid false accusations from war zones or during the victim's minor age.

Key Terms
مطالبة (mutalabah): Demand by the victim for the hadd punishment to be carried out.
تقادم (taqadum): The passage of time; oldness of the alleged zina that prevents acceptance of witness testimony.
محصن (muhsan): A chaste person who is free, adult, and Muslim, and has not been convicted of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a condition for hadd al-qadhf?
A) The victim must be unmarried.
B) The accuser must be a Muslim.
C) The victim must demand the punishment.
D) The accusation must be witnessed by two people.

Key Takeaway
Hadd al-qadhf is only applied when the victim is muhsan, demands punishment, and the accusation is explicitly of zina. Comparative phrases like 'أنت أزنى' are subject to dispute.

Imprisonment of a Witness in Qadhf Cases: A Procedural Ruling
Ruling on detaining a witness who claims distance prevents timely production of the accused.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on detaining a witness in a qadhf case when the accused is within or beyond a three-day travel distance, and explain the rationale behind the uniform imprisonment.

Core Idea
Imprison the witness regardless of distance – proximity does not excuse detention.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq quotes two later Hanafi fatwa works, al-Khaniya and al-Zahiriyya, on a procedural point: when a witness in a qadhf case claims he can bring the accused to court, the judge must imprison him. The rule applies uniformly whether the accused is near (within three days' travel) or far. This ensures the witness does not abscond and the case proceeds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is imprisoning the witness who claims to be able to bring the accused for qadhf. The ruling is that imprisonment is wajib (obligatory) in both scenarios.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the evidence comes from later fatwa works.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario 1: The place is far, so the witness cannot bring the accused within three days → imprison. Scenario 2: The place is near, so the witness can bring him within three days → also imprison.
The three-day measure is a standard travel distance in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Note the authority
The ruling is from al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniya, which are later fatwa collections (fatawa mutakhkhirin). These are relied upon in practice, though not part of Zahir al-Riwaya.
Know the hierarchy: Zahir al-Riwaya > Nawadir > Fatawa Mutakhkhirin.
4
Understand the rationale
Imprisonment is precautionary: even if the accused is near, the witness might still flee or fail to produce him. Detention secures his presence.
This is a procedural measure, not a punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحبسه؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي الظهيرية هذا إذا كان المكان الذي فيه الشاهد بعيداً من المصر بحيث لا يمكنه الإحضار في ثلاثة أيام، أما إذا كان المكان قريباً يمكنه الإحضار في ثلاثة أيام فإنه يحبسه أيضاً.
He imprisons him; thus in al-Khaniya. And in al-Zahiriyya: This is when the place where the witness is is far from the city such that he cannot bring him within three days. But if the place is near such that he can bring him within three days, then he also imprisons him.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the fatwa collections al-Khaniya and al-Zahiriyya concerning the procedure when a witness in a qadhf case claims he can bring the accused to court. The ruling is that the judge should imprison the witness regardless of the distance of the accused. Even if the accused is near enough to be brought within three days, the witness is still imprisoned. This ensures that the witness does not flee and that justice is served. The ruling is based on the authority of these later Hanafi fatwa works, not the foundational texts.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse).
شاهد (shahid): A witness who comes forward to testify to the qadhf or to the zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zahiriyya, if the witness can bring the accused within three days, what does the judge do?
A) Release the witness without bail
B) Imprison the witness
C) Accept the witness's word and delay the case
D) Fine the witness

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa practice, a witness in a qadhf case is imprisoned to ensure he produces the accused, irrespective of the distance.

Accepting Witness Testimony with Minor Inconsistencies in Qadhf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting testimony with day or type discrepancy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding witness testimony in qadhf when there is a minor discrepancy in details, and explain the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
Minor inconsistencies in testimony do not invalidate qadhf evidence according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn require exact correspondence.

This passage from al-Zahiriyya presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when two witnesses testify about a qadhf but vary in detail (e.g., different days or one testifies to an acknowledgment vs. direct statement), should their testimony be accepted? Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how the Hanafi school balances strictness with practical flexibility in hadd cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
Determine the exact inconsistency in the witnesses' testimony: difference in the day of the event, or one testifies to a direct statement and the other to an acknowledgment.
The passage gives two parallel scenarios.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa accepts the testimony despite the discrepancy. His view is that the essence of the qadhf is established, and minor differences do not undermine the accusation.
The text says: 'قال أبو حنيفة : تقبل هذه الشهادة'
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad reject the testimony. They require exact correspondence in the witnesses' accounts for the hadd penalty to be applied.
The text says: 'وقالا : لا تقبل'
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the hadd penalty for qadhf is applied. Under the Sahibayn, the testimony is insufficient, so the qadhif escapes punishment.
This difference directly affects whether the hadd is carried out.
5
Note the source and authority weight
The dispute is recorded in al-Zahiriyya, a later fatwa collection. It is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf within the Zahir al-Riwayah.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is not explicitly stated in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية أيضاً : إذا ادعى رجل على رجل أنه قذفه وجاء بشاهدين فالقاضي يسأل الشاهدين عن القذف ما هو وكيف هو، فإذا قالا نشهد أنه قال له يا زاني قبلت شهادتهما وحد القاذف إن كانا عدلين فإن شهد أحدهما أنه قال له يا زاني يوم وشهد الآخر أنه قال له يا زاني يوم الخميس قال أبو حنيفة : تقبل هذه الشهادة. وقالا : لا تقبل، وكذا لو شهد أحدهما بالإقرار والآخر بالإنشاء اهـ.
And in al-Zahiriyya also: If a man claims that another man qadhafa him and brings two witnesses, the judge asks the witnesses about the qadhf: what it is and how it is. If they both say 'We testify that he said to him, 'O fornicator,' then their testimony is accepted and the qadhif is punished with hadd if they are just. But if one testifies that he said to him 'O fornicator' on a certain day, and the other testifies that he said to him 'O fornicator' on Thursday, Abu Hanifa said: This testimony is accepted. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not accepted. Similarly, if one testifies to an acknowledgment (iqrar) and the other to a direct statement (insha), then [the same difference].
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the acceptance of witness testimony in qadhf cases when the witnesses' accounts vary. The scenario: two witnesses testify that a man said 'O fornicator' to the plaintiff, but one says it was on an unspecified day and the other says it was on a specific day (Thursday). Abu Hanifa accepts the testimony, considering the discrepancy minor and not affecting the substance of the qadhf. The Sahibayn reject it, requiring consistency in the details. The same rule applies if one witness testifies to a direct statement of qadhf and the other testifies that the defendant acknowledged committing qadhf. The dispute is reported from al-Zahiriyya, a later fatwa collection. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the one being explained.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court, specifically regarding the occurrence of qadhf.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession, here referring to the defendant acknowledging that he committed qadhf.
إنشاء (insha): The original utterance of the qadhf itself, as opposed to an acknowledgment of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where one witness testifies that the defendant said 'ya zani' on an unspecified day and the other says on Thursday, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted and the hadd is applied
B) The testimony is rejected due to discrepancy
C) Only one witness is needed for hadd
D) The case is dismissed

Key Takeaway
In qadhf, Abu Hanifa accepts testimony with minor inconsistencies (e.g., in the day or between iqrar and insha), while the Sahibayn reject it; the practical effect is whether the hadd is applied or not.

Conditions for Hadd in Qadhf: Muhsan and Proof Requirement
Commentary on the matn: the hadd for qadhf requires the victim to be muhsan and the qadhib unable to prove the zina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the hadd of qadhf and apply the ruling when the qadhib produces evidence of old versus recent zina.

Core Idea
Hadd for qadhf requires a muhsan victim and the accuser's inability to prove the accusation.

This lesson unpacks a key commentary on the Hanafi ruling for qadhf (false accusation of zina). The commentator clarifies that the hadd only applies when the victim is muhsan (free, adult, Muslim, chaste) and the accuser cannot bring four witnesses. We will also explore what happens if the accuser does produce witnesses, especially when the zina is old, using an analogy from pre-accusation testimony.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling and primary dalil
Identify the ruling that hadd applies only to accusing a muhsan, and cite the Quranic verse (24:4) as the primary proof. Note that the verse mentions muhsanat and the requirement of four witnesses.
The consensus (ijma) also supports this.
2
Define muhsan for qadhf
List the four attributes of a muhsan in this context: free, adult, Muslim, and chaste (never convicted of zina). Explain why each is necessary for the hadd to apply.
Accusing a non-muhsan (e.g., slave, non-Muslim) does not carry the hadd.
3
Understand the condition of the qadhib's inability to prove
The commentator notes that mentioning muhsan implicitly covers this condition, because if the qadhib proves the zina, the victim is no longer muhsan. The verse also requires four witnesses.
If the qadhib brings four witnesses, the hadd falls.
4
Analyze the qiyas on old zina (mutaqadim)
Examine the analogy from al-Zahiriyya: if witnesses testify to old zina before the qadhf, neither the accuser nor the victim is punished. The same applies if they testify after, based on the illa of the zina being old.
The illa (effective cause) is the oldness of the zina, which prevents the hadd from being applied.
5
Apply the reasoning to distinguish old vs. recent zina
Practice determining the outcome when the qadhib produces witnesses: if the zina is old, neither is punished; if it is recent, the victim (if muhsan) is punished for zina, and the qadhib is not punished for qadhf.
This distinction is crucial for accurate fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو قذف محصناً أو محصنة بزنا حد بطلبه (مفرقاً أي بطلب المقذوف مفرقاً على أعضاء القاذف لما تلوناه من الآية وبينا من الإجماع قيد بالمحصن لأن غيره لا يجب الحد بقذفه، وفيه إشارة إلى اشتراط عجز القاذف عن إقامة البينة على الزنا فإنه إذا أقام بينة على صدق مقالته لم يبق المقذوف محصناً فأغنى ذكر الإحصان عن هذا الشرط، وكذا لو صدقه المقذوف، وفي الظهيرية : رجل قذف رجلاً بالزنا فرفعه المقذوف إلى القاضي فقال القاذف عندي شهود عدول على ما قلت وأقامهم على ذلك فإنه لا يحد. وهل يحد المقذوف؟ إن شهدوا بحد متقادم فإنه لا يحد كما لو شهدوا عليه بالزنا قبل القذف إن كان متقادماً لم يحد، وإن كان غير متقادم حد فكذلك ههنا .اهـ.
His statement: 'So if he qadhafa a muhsan (chaste) man or a muhsana woman with zina, he is punished with hadd upon his request' — i.e., upon the request of the one qadhfed, distributed over the limbs of the qadhif, because of what we recited from the verse and what we explained from consensus. He restricted it with 'muhsan' because for other than him the hadd is not obligatory by qadhfing him. And in it is an indication of the condition that the qadhif is unable to establish evidence of zina, because if he produces evidence of the truthfulness of his statement, the qadhfed is no longer muhsan. So mentioning ihsan suffices from this condition. Likewise, if the qadhfed confirms him. And in al-Zahiriyya: A man qadhafa a man with zina, and the qadhfed raised it to the judge. The qadhif said, 'I have just witnesses for what I said,' and he brought them for that — then he is not punished with hadd. And is the qadhfed punished? If they testify to a past hadd (i.e., an old zina), then he is not punished, just as if they had testified against him of zina before the qadhf — if it was old, he is not punished, and if it was not old, he is punished. So likewise here.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the ruling on qadhf. The matn states that if someone accuses a muhsan (chaste, free, adult Muslim) of zina, the hadd (80 lashes) is applied upon the request of the victim. The commentator explains the condition of muhsan: the hadd is only for accusing a muhsan; accusing a non-muhsan (e.g., a slave, an unbeliever, or someone known for fornication) does not carry the hadd. The commentator also draws an implication: the qadhif must be unable to prove the zina. If he can prove it (by bringing four witnesses), the victim loses his muhsan status and the hadd falls. This is further elaborated by a citation from al-Zahiriyya: if the qadhif brings witnesses after the accusation, he is not punished. If the witnesses testify to an old act of zina (prior to the qadhif's accusation), the victim is not punished either, by analogy with the rule that a person who confesses to an old zina is not subject to hadd. The proof for the ruling is the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-Nur, 24:4) and the consensus of the scholars.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, Muslim, and has never committed zina (i.e., is chaste).
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment of 80 lashes for falsely accusing a muhsan of zina.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, specifically four male witnesses to the actual act of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the qadhif brings witnesses after accusing someone, and they testify to an old (mutaqadim) act of zina by the victim?
A) Both the qadhif and the victim are punished with hadd
B) The qadhif is not punished, and the victim is not punished for zina
C) The qadhif is punished, but the victim is not
D) The qadhif is not punished, but the victim is punished for zina

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf is only applied when the victim is muhsan and the accuser cannot produce four witnesses; if the accuser proves an old zina, neither party faces hadd.

Hanafi Rulings on Specific Wordings of Qadhf
States multiple rulings on qadhf based on wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for specific wordings of qadhf, including gender-mismatched, ambiguous, and animal-related accusations.

Core Idea
Not every accusation of zina triggers the hadd; wording, context, and status determine the punishment.

This lesson covers key rulings from the Bahr al-Raiq on qadhf. The passage lists numerous scenarios where the wording or context affects whether the hadd penalty applies. Understanding these nuances is critical for anyone dealing with hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify Categories
Categorize the accusations into gender-mismatched, ambiguous/group, and animal-related. This helps apply consistent rules.
2
Apply the Directness Principle
If the wording is a clear, direct accusation of zina, hadd applies. Indirect or ambiguous wordings generally do not incur hadd.
For example, 'you are a formicator' is direct; 'I have not seen a better fornicator' is indirect.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
On using the feminine form for a man, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no hadd; Muhammad says it is qadhf. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
This distinction shows the importance of gender agreement.
4
Analyze Connected vs. Disconnected Speech
In group testimony, if the phrase 'within the private part' is said connectedly, no hadd; if separated, hadd applies. This hinges on whether the statement explicitly negates full zina.
Connected speech clarifies the accusation as incomplete.
5
Evaluate Animal-Related Accusations
When the animal is one not typically used for zina (e.g., camel, bull), no hadd. When the animal or object is typically associated (e.g., female camel, dirham), hadd applies due to implied zina with a person.
The letter 'ba' can imply exchange, leading to a possible innocent interpretation, but the counter-interpretation prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه. ولو قال لرجل يا زانية بالتاء لا يحد في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وقال محمد: يكون قاذفاً. ولو قال لامرأة يا زاني يجب الحد في قولهم لأنه ترخيم وهو حذف آخر الكلمة. ولو قال لرجل زان لا حد عليه، ولو قال لأهل قرية ليس فيكم زان إلا واحداً أو قال كلكم زان إلا واحداً أو قال لرجلين أحدكما زان فقيل هذا لأحدهما بعينه فقال نعم صدقت هو [؟] حد عليه. ولو قال لرجل يا زاني فقال له غيره صدقت حد المبتدئ دون المصدق . ولو قال له كما قلت فهو قاذف أيضاً. ولو أن جماعة قالوا رأينا فلاناً يزني بفلانة ثم قالوا فيما دون الفرج متصلاً لا حد على المقذوف ولا على الجماعة، ولو قطعوا الكلام ثم قالوا فيما دون الفرج كان عليهم حد القذف ولو قال من قال كذا وكذا فهو ابن الزانية فقال رجل أنا قلت لا حد على المبتدئ. ولو قال لغيره أنت تزني لا حد عليه. ولو قال لامرأة ما رأيت زانية خيراً منك لا حد عليه ولو قال لامرأة زنى بك زوجك قبل أن يتزوجك كان قاذفاً. ولو قال لغيره زنى فخذك أو ظهرك أو يدك لا حد عليه. ولو قال زني فرجك كان قاذفاً. ولو قذف رجلاً بغير لسان العربية كان عليه الحد. ولو قال لغيره أخبرت أنك زان أو قال أشهدت على ذلك لا حد عليه. ولو قال لغيره زنيت وفلان معك يكون قاذفاً لهما. ولو قال عنيت وفلان معك شاهد لا يصدق. ولو قال أشهد أنك زان فقال رجل آخر وأنا أشهد أيضاً لا حد على الثاني إلا أن يقول وأنا أشهد عليه بمثل ما شهدت به عليه فحينئذ يكون قاذفاً. ولو قال لغيره اذهب إلى فلان وقل له يا زاني فلا حد على الآمر. وهل يحد المأمور؟ إن كان المأمور قال له يا زاني يحد، وإن قال له إن فلاناً يقول لك يا زاني لم يحد. ولو قال لآخر يابن الزانية وهذا معك قال ذلك بكلام واحد فهذا ليس بقذف للثاني. ولو قال لرجل يا زاني وهذا معك كان قاذفاً لهما. ولو قال لآخر يابن الزانية وهذا ولم يقل معك فهو قاذف للثاني. رجل قال لامرأة أجنبية زنيت ببعير أو بثور أو بحمار لا حد عليه لأنه نسبها إلى التمكين من البهائم، ولو قال زنيت بناقة أو ببقرة أو بثوب أو بدرهم فعليه الحد لأن معنی کلامه زنیت بناقة بذلت لك أو بدرهم بذل لك في الزنا. فإن قيل: بل معنی کلامه زنیت بدرهم استؤجرت عليه فينبغي أن لا يحد في قول أبي حنيفة، وهذا لأن حرف الباء تصحب الأعواض والأبدال قيل له : هذا محتمل وما ذكرناه محتمل فيتقابل المحتملان ويبقى قوله زنيت لم يزذ على هذا. ولو قال لرجل زنيت ببعير أو بناقة أو ما أشبه ذلك لا حد عليه لأنه
For him. And if a man says to a man 'O adulteress' (feminine) with the ta, he is not flogged according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: He is a slanderer. And if he says to a woman 'O adulterer' (masculine), the hadd is wajib in their view because it is tarikhim, which is omission of the last letter. And if he says to a man 'adulterer', there is no hadd upon him. And if he says to the people of a village 'there is no adulterer among you except one' or says 'all of you are adulterers except one' or says to two men 'one of you is an adulterer', and he says 'this is intended for a specific one of them' and he says 'yes, you have spoken the truth', he is flogged. And if he says to a man 'O adulterer' and another says to him 'you have spoken the truth', the initiator is flogged but not the one who affirms. And if he says to him 'like what you said' then he is also a slanderer. And if a group says 'we saw so-and-so committing zina with so-and-so' and then they say 'within the private part' connectedly, there is no hadd upon the accused nor upon the group; and if they separate the speech and then say 'within the private part', the hadd of qadhf is upon them. And if a man says 'whoever said such-and-such is the son of an adulteress' and a man says 'I said it', there is no hadd on the initiator. And if he says to another 'you are committing zina', there is no hadd upon him. And if he says to a woman 'I have not seen an adulteress better than you', there is no hadd upon him. And if he says to a woman 'your husband committed zina with you before marrying you', he is a slanderer. And if he says to another 'you committed zina with your thigh, back, or hand', there is no hadd upon him. And if he says 'you committed zina with your private part', he is a slanderer. And if he slanders a man in a non-Arabic tongue, the hadd is upon him. And if he says to another 'I have been told you are an adulterer' or 'I testify to that', there is no hadd upon him. And if he says to another 'you committed zina and so-and-so was with you', he is a slanderer toward both. And if he says 'I meant and so-and-so is a witness', he is not believed. And if he says 'I testify that you are an adulterer' and another man says 'I also testify', there is no hadd on the second unless he says 'I also testify against him with the same testimony', then he is a slanderer. And if he says to another 'go to so-and-so and say to him O adulterer', there is no hadd on the commander. And is the commanded one flogged? If the commanded one says to him 'O adulterer', he is flogged; and if he says 'so-and-so says to you O adulterer', he is not flogged. And if he says to another 'O son of an adulteress, and this one is with you' uttered in one phrase, this is not a qadhf of the second. And if he says to a man 'O adulterer, and this one is with you', he is a slanderer toward both. And if he says to another 'O son of an adulteress, and this one' without saying 'with you', he is a slanderer of the second. A man said to a foreign woman 'you committed zina with a camel, or a bull, or a donkey' – no hadd upon him because he attributed her to enabling beasts; and if he says 'you committed zina with a female camel, or a cow, or a cloth, or a dirham', the hadd is upon him because the meaning of his speech is 'you committed zina with a female camel that you gave' or 'with a dirham that you gave in zina'. For if it is said: rather the meaning of his speech is 'you committed zina with a dirham for which you were hired', so it should be that he is not flogged according to Abu Hanifa, and this is because the letter 'ba' accompanies compensations and substitutes. It is said to him: this is possible, and what we mentioned is possible, so the two possibilities counterbalance, and his saying 'you committed zina' remains without addition to this. And if he says to a man 'you committed zina with a camel, or a female camel, or the like', there is no hadd upon him because
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the Sharh of Kanz al-Daqaiq on the chapter of qadhf (slanderous accusation of zina). It lists various wordings and whether they incur the hadd penalty. The rulings are given without explicit proofs, serving as a memorization anchor. Key points: using the feminine ta for a man exempts hadd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad disagrees. Addressing a woman with masculine form incurs hadd as it is considered tarikhim. Ambiguous statements like 'one of you is an adulterer' may not incur hadd unless clarified. The ruling on testimony interrupted by 'within the private part' depends on whether the speech was connected. Accusations involving animals: if the animal is not typically used for intercourse (camel, bull, donkey), no hadd; if it is a female camel or pillow, etc., hadd is due. The commentary also discusses the debate over the meaning of 'ba' as a substitute.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina or illegitimacy
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment for certain crimes, including 80 lashes for qadhf
إحصان (ihsan): The condition of being a free, adult, Muslim, and chaste person for whom qadhf hadd is applicable
ترخيم (tarakhim): Omission of the last letter of a word, often used in calling out, e.g., 'ya Zainab' for 'ya Zainabu'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man says to a woman 'زنيت بثور' (you committed zina with a bull), what is the ruling?
A) He is flogged with 80 lashes.
B) He is not flogged.
C) He is flogged only if the woman is muhsana.
D) He is flogged because the bull is a domestic animal.

Key Takeaway
The hadd penalty for qadhf is strictly applied based on clear and direct wording; ambiguous statements or those with possible innocent interpretations do not incur the hadd.

Conditions for Hadd in Qadhf: Ihsan, Demand, and Physical Possibility
Commentary on conditions of hadd and bestiality accusations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three key conditions for qadhf hadd (ihsan, victim's demand, possibility of zina) and apply them to cases involving a mute or physically incapable person.

Core Idea
Hadd for qadhf only applies when the victim can be disgraced; impossibility bars punishment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the nuanced conditions for the hadd penalty in false accusations of zina. While a false accusation is a grave sin, the hadd is not automatic—it is a right of the victim that depends on their ability to be dishonored and their explicit demand for punishment. We will break down the key conditions: the victim's ihsan (chastity), the requirement of a demand, and the physical possibility of the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational conditions for qadhf hadd
From the text, note that the victim must be a free, adult, Muslim, and chaste (muhsan). Also, the hadd is only carried out if the victim demands it, as it is primarily their right.
Ihsan must exist at the time of the hadd, not at the time of the accusation.
2
Examine the exception for physical impossibility
The text states that if the victim is a ratqa' (imperforate) or majbub (castrated), no hadd is due because the accusation is obviously false and no disgrace attaches.
The rationale is that the hadd is to remove disgrace; if the claim is visibly false, disgrace does not occur.
3
Analyze the case of a mute victim
The mute cannot verbally demand hadd; his gesture is insufficient. The text suggests that if he could speak, he might have confirmed the accuser, so no hadd.
This highlights that demand is an active, verbal requirement.
4
Apply the condition of victim's zina before hadd
If the victim commits zina or apostatizes before the hadd is carried out, the hadd falls, because the victim's ihsan is a condition that must persist.
Even if they later repent or return to Islam, the hadd is not reinstated.
5
Synthesize the conditions into a checklist
List: 1) Victim must be muhsan at time of hadd. 2) Victim must demand the hadd verbally. 3) The act of zina must be possible for the victim (not ratqa/majbub). If any condition is missing, no hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ينزع غير الفرو والحشو وإحصانه بكونه مكلفاً حراً مسلماً عفيفاً عن الزنا فلو قال نسبه إلى إتيان البهيمة، فإن قال بأمة أو دار أو ثوب فعليه الحد؛ كذا في الخانية والظهيرية . وبه تبين أن حد القذف لا يجب مع التصريح بالزنا في بعض المسائل لقرينة، ويجب في بعض المسائل مع عدم التصريح مثل ما تقدم من قوله هو كما قال فحينئذ يحتاج إلى ضبط هذه المسألة. وفي الخانية : رجل قال لغيره يا لوطي لا حد عليه، ولو نسبه إلى اللواطة صريحاً لا حد عليه في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال صاحباه يحد .اهـ. واعلم أنه يشترط وجود الإحصان وقت الحد حتى لو زنى المقذوف قبل أن يقام الحد على القاذف أوطئ وطئاً حراماً على ما ذكرنا أو ارتد والعياذ بالله تعالى سقط الحد عن القاذف، ولو أسلم بعد ذلك لأن إحصان المقذوف شرط فلا بد من وجوده عند إقامة الحد؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وقيد بطلبه لأنه حقه وينتفع به على الخصوص من حيث دفع العار على نفسه وإن كان الغالب فيه حق الله تعالى على الأصح. وأشار به إلى أن قذف الأخرس لا يوجب الحد لأن طلبه يكون بالإشارة ولعله لو كان ينطق لصدقه ولما كان الطلب، ثم الحد لدفع العار استفيد منه أنه لا بد من تصور الزنا من المقذوف حتى لو قذف رتقاء أو مجبوباً لا يجب عليه الحد لأنهما لا يلحقهما العار بذلك لظهور كذبه بيقين . قوله بحمار أو بعير إدخال ذكره في قبل مشتهاة إلى آخره بخلاف ما لو قال زنيت بناقة أو أتان أو دراهم لأن معناه زنيت وأخذت البدل إذ لا تصلح المذكورات للإدخال في فرجها ولو قيل هذا الرجل لا يحد لأنه ليس العرف في جانبه أخذ المال .اهـ. وهو مخالف لما ذكره المؤلف فإن هذا التعليل يفيد أنه لو قال له زنيت بدار أو ثوب أن لا يحد كما لو قال له بدراهم إلا أن تكون الإشارة بقوله : «ولو قيل هذا الرجل إلى أو ثور» تأمل. ثم رأيت في كافي الحاكم : وإن قال لرجل زنيت ببعير أو بناقة أو ما أشبه ذلك أو بأمة لم يحد إلا في الأمة خاصة .اهـ.
And the condition of being a free, adult, Muslim, and chaste from zina is not removed except by fornication and compresses? [؟]. So if he says he attributes him to bestiality, then if he says 'with a slave-girl, house, or cloth', the hadd is upon him; thus in al-Khaniyya and al-Zuhayriyya. And by this it becomes clear that the hadd of qadhf is not wajib despite explicit mention of zina in some cases due to a contextual indication, and it is wajib in some cases without explicit mention, like what preceded from his saying 'as he said'; so then one needs to establish this issue. And in al-Khaniyya: A man said to another 'O sodomite', no hadd upon him; and if he attributes him to sodomy explicitly, no hadd upon him according to Abu Hanifa. And know that it is a condition that ihsan exist at the time of the hadd, so that if the accused committed zina before the hadd is carried out on the accuser, or he engaged in forbidden intercourse, as we mentioned, or he apostatized (may Allah protect), the hadd falls from the accuser, even if he later becomes Muslim, because the ihsan of the accused is a condition, so it must exist at the time of carrying out the hadd; thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is conditioned on his demand because it is his right and he benefits from it specifically in terms of removing disgrace from himself, even though predominantly it is the right of Allah according to the most correct view. A statement: 'with a donkey or camel' means he inserted his penis into the private part of a desirous female? But not if he said 'with a female camel or donkey or dirhams' because its meaning is he committed zina and took the compensation, since the mentioned items are not suitable for insertion into her private part; and if it is said 'this man is not flogged because the custom on his side is not taking money.' Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from the sharh of the matn. It begins by discussing the conditions for hadd, specifically ihsan (chastity). It then addresses the ruling on accusing someone of bestiality: if the object is not typically used for intercourse (e.g., a house, cloth), hadd is due because it implies actual zina with that object. The text from al-Khaniyya discusses sodomy accusations. Then it discusses the condition that ihsan must exist at the time of hadd, and that the victim's demand is required. The mute cannot demand, so no hadd. Also, if the accused is physically incapable of zina (e.g., ra'qa, majbub), no hadd because the accusation is obviously false. The final part is a commentary on a specific phrase in the matn regarding bestiality, reconciling different views from al-Nahr and Kafi al-Hakim.

Key Terms
رتقاء (ratqa'): A woman with an imperforate hymen, essentially incapable of vaginal intercourse
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis is cut off, incapable of intercourse
إحصان (ihsan): The condition of being free, adult, Muslim, and chaste (never committed zina)

Key Takeaway
Hadd for qadhf is conditional on the victim's ihsan at the time of execution, their demand, and the physical possibility of the act; without any of these, no hadd is imposed.

Qadhf of Bestiality and Sodomy: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Object Interpretation
Commentary on conditions of hadd and bestiality accusations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on accusing someone of bestiality and sodomy, including the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on sodomy, and apply the rule that hadd depends on the type of object mentioned.

Core Idea
Words matter: bestiality accusations incur hadd only if the object can physically be used for intercourse.

The passage deepens into two nuanced areas of qadhf: accusing someone of bestiality (zina with an animal) and sodomy (liwat). The author examines which objects trigger hadd and which do not, and presents an important intra-Hanafi disagreement on sodomy. Understanding these distinctions refines one's grasp of how the law treats implicit vs explicit accusations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for bestiality accusations
The matn states that if a person says 'You committed zina with a slave-girl, house, or cloth', hadd is due. The reasoning is that these objects are not suitable for actual intercourse, so the accusation implies zina with a human.
The commentary provides a contradictory view from Kafi al-Hakim that only the slave-girl incurs hadd.
2
Analyze the sodomy disagreement
The text from al-Khaniyya: Abu Hanifa holds that explicit accusation of sodomy (liwat) does not incur hadd, while his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does. Note the positions.
The dispute hinges on whether sodomy is considered zina for the purpose of qadhf.
3
Evaluate the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa likely argues that the word 'zina' in the Quranic hadd verse specifically refers to vaginal intercourse; sodomy is a different act. Therefore, accusing someone of sodomy does not directly accuse them of zina.
The companions may argue that linguistically, sodomy is a form of zina and the slander is equally defamatory.
4
Apply the distinction to animal objects
The commentary gives examples: 'with a donkey/camel' implies actual insertion, so hadd; 'with a female camel/donkey/dirhams' does not because these objects are not used for insertion and imply a different meaning (taking money).
The hadd is only when the statement can be reasonably interpreted as accusing of zina with a human.
5
Resolve the contradiction between matn and Kafi al-Hakim
The matn says hadd for 'with a house or cloth', but Kafi al-Hakim says no hadd except for slave-girl. The commentator notes this contradiction and leaves it for the student to contemplate.
Stronger evidence: Kafi al-Hakim's view may be more restrictive, but the matn's rule is more common in later Hanafi fatwa.

It then addresses the ruling on accusing someone of bestiality: if the object is not typically used for intercourse (e.g., a house, cloth), hadd is due because it implies actual zina with that object. The text from al-Khaniyya discusses sodomy accusations. Then it discusses the condition that ihsan must exist at the time of hadd, and that the victim's demand is required. The mute cannot demand, so no hadd. Also, if the accused is physically incapable of zina (e.g., ra'qa, majbub), no hadd because the accusation is obviously false. The final part is a commentary on a specific phrase in the matn regarding bestiality, reconciling different views from al-Nahr and Kafi al-Hakim.

Key Terms
لوطي (luti): One who commits sodomy; the term is used as an insult.
اللواط (al-liwat): Sodomy (anal intercourse); a sin but legally distinct from zina in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, does an explicit accusation of sodomy (liwat) incur hadd for qadhf?
A) Yes, because sodomy is a form of zina.
B) No, because the hadd is specifically for false accusation of zina.
C) Yes, if the victim is muhsan.
D) No, because sodomy accusations are always false.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the hadd for qadhf applies to bestiality accusations only when the object implies zina with a human; sodomy accusations do not incur hadd according to Abu Hanifa's relied-upon view.

Hadd for Qadhf of Incapable Persons: The Rule and Its Critical Refinement
Super-commentary refining qadhf rulings for eunuchs, slaves, and hermaphrodites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on qadhf of persons incapable of zina, identify the disputed categories, and apply the commentator's refinement regarding the hermaphrodite.

Core Idea
Hadd for qadhf depends on the accused's physical capability for zina, not marital status.

This lesson examines a nuance in the law of qadhf: what happens when the accused is incapable of zina? The classical Hanafi texts exempt some categories, but the super-commentary critiques the reasoning and offers a refined position for eunuchs, slaves, and hermaphrodites. We will follow the argument step by step, paying close attention to the distinction between impossibility and mere uncertainty of zina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule and its exceptions
Start with the general principle: qadhf requires the ability of the accused to commit zina. Note the categories initially exempted (ratqa', majbub) and those added in al-Nahr (eunuch, slave).
The base rule is that hadd is not wajib if the accused is physically incapable of zina.
2
Analyze the reasoning for each category
For eunuchs and impotent men, zina is not impossible, so hadd may apply. For ratqa' and majbub, zina is impossible (absence of genitalia). For slaves, the rule is absolute: no hadd regardless of capability, as per al-Hamawi.
Distinguish categories based on physical possibility versus legal status.
3
Critique the reasoning for hermaphrodites
The commentator rejects the argument that a hermaphrodite's suspended marriage negates hadd. Marriage is irrelevant for qadhf; only the possibility of zina matters. Since a hermaphrodite could potentially engage in zina, hadd is wajib.
The key insight: hadd for qadhf is independent of ihsan (marital status used in stoning).
4
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The commentator concludes that hadd is wajib for qadhf of eunuchs and hermaphrodites because zina is not definitively impossible. For slaves, the ruling remains no hadd absolutely.
This is the operative position for fatwa, per the commentator's tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (حتى لو قذف رتقاء أو محبوباً لا يجب عليه الحد) زاد في النهر في قذف من لا يجب بقذفه الحد الخصي والمملوك للقاذف كما سيأتي والخنثى الذي بلغ مشكلاً نص عليه في السراجية ووجهه أن نكاجه موقوف وهو لا يفيد الحل اهـ. وفيه نظر ; ففي التتارخانية وكذلك إذا قذف الرتقاء لا حد عليه وكانت بمنزلة المجبوب بخلاف ما لو قذف خصياً أو عنيناً لأن الزنا منهما غير منتف وكذا إذا قذف امرأة عذراء لأن الزنا متصور فكان الصواب ترك الخصي وكذا المملوك لما في حاشية مسكين عن الحموي أن الذي سيأتي ما إذا قذف أم مملوكه وأما المملوك فقذفه لا يوجب الحد مطلقاً، سواء كان مملوكه أو مملوك غيره كما سيأتي في التعزير. واعترض الحموي أيضاً تعليله بمسألة الخنثى بأنه لا دخل للنكاح البات المفيد للحل في إيجاب حد القذف حتى يترتب على عدمه عدم وجوب الحد وإنما ذاك في حد الزنا بالرجم اهـ . قلت : بل لا دخل للنكاح أصلاً قال في الدر المختار: ينقص عن إحصان الرجم بشين النكاح والدخول . قلت والظاهر وجوب الحد بقذفه لعدم تحقق الزنا منه لاحتمال زيادة كل من السلعتين اهـ.
His statement: 'Even if he slanders a ratqa' or a majbub, the hadd is not wajib upon him.' Added in al-Nahr regarding qadhf of one against whom the hadd is not wajib: the eunuch and the slave owned by the accuser, as will come, and the hermaphrodite who has reached puberty ambiguously, as stated in al-Sirajiyya, and its reasoning is that his marriage is suspended and does not achieve the permissible. End of quote. There is consideration in it: In al-Tatarkhaniyya: Likewise, if he slanders a ratqa', no hadd upon him, and she is in the position of the majbub, contrary to if he slanders a eunuch or an impotent man because zina from them is not impossible. Likewise, if he slanders a virgin woman because zina is conceivable. So the correct thing is to omit the eunuch. Likewise, the slave, according to what is in the marginal note of Miskin from al-Hamawi: that what will come is if he slanders the slave mother of his child; as for the slave, his qadhf does not necessitate hadd absolutely, whether it be his own slave or another's slave, as will come in ta'zir. And al-Hamawi also objected to his reasoning in the issue of the hermaphrodite: that there is no role of permanent marriage that achieves permissibility in necessitating the hadd of qadhf such that its absence leads to absence of hadd; rather, that is in the hadd of zina by stoning. I say: Rather, there is no role of marriage at all. He said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The hadd for qadhf is deficient compared to the hadd of stoning by the ugliness of marriage and intercourse. I say: And the apparent is the obligation of hadd for his qadhf due to the lack of certainty of zina from him due to the possibility of increase of both items.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement, a super-commentary on the sharh discussing whether hadd applies when the accused is incapable of zina (e.g., eunuch, slave, hermaphrodite). The text from al-Nahr added the categories of eunuch and slave owned by the accuser. Al-Tatarkhaniyya distinguishes between eunuch/impotent (zina possible) and ratqa'/majbub (impossible). The commentator challenges the reasoning on hermaphrodites, stating that marriage is irrelevant for qadhf hadd. The final opinion from al-Durr al-Mukhtar suggests hadd should be wajib for qadhf of a hermaphrodite because zina is not certain to be impossible. The discussion reflects the nuanced Hanafi approach to ensuring that only clearly false accusations incur hadd.

Key Terms
خصي (khasi): A eunuch; a castrated man
خنثى (khuntha): A hermaphrodite with ambiguous genitals

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's final opinion, why should hadd be wajib for qadhf of a hermaphrodite (khuntha)?
A) Because a hermaphrodite can contract a valid marriage.
B) Because zina from a hermaphrodite is not definitively impossible.
C) Because the accuser's statement is a clear slander.
D) Because the hadd for qadhf is independent of marriage.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi law of qadhf considers the physical capability for zina as a condition for the hadd to be due; where zina is not impossible, the accuser may be liable.
