Accusation of Liwat: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Hadd al-Qadhf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liwat accusation and conditions for qadhf hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether accusing someone of liwat incurs the hadd of qadhf, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and explain the conditions that must be present for the hadd to be established.

Core Idea
Accusing of liwat: Abu Hanifa says no hadd; the Sahibayn say yes, because only zina triggers qadhf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a key intra-Hanafi disagreement: does accusing someone of sodomy (liwat) trigger the fixed punishment (hadd) for false accusation (qadhf)? While the Qur'an specifies the hadd for accusing chaste persons of zina, the Hanafi masters divided on whether liwat falls under that ruling. The passage also explains important conditions for the hadd to apply, such as the victim's demand and the possibility of zina. Let's trace the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the common ground
Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree on the basic rules of qadhf for accusing of zina. The dispute is only about liwat.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
No hadd for accusing of liwat, whether by saying 'ya loti' or explicitly.
The text says 'la hadda 'alayhi' (no hadd upon him) in the opinion of Abu Hanifa.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Hadd is incurred for accusing of liwat.
The text says 'qala sahibahu: yuhadd' (his two companions said: he is subject to hadd).
4
Analyze the underlying legal distinction
Abu Hanifa distinguishes liwat from zina; the Quranic text for qadhf (Surah al-Nur: 4) specifies those who accuse 'chaste women' (al-muhsanat) of zina. The Sahibayn analogize liwat to zina because both are unlawful sexual acts that bring equal disgrace.
The passage does not give explicit proofs, but this distinction is well-known in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the conditions for hadd
Even if the Sahibayn's view is taken, the hadd is only established if (a) the victim demands it (talab), (b) the victim is capable of zina (so accusing a ratqa' or majbub does not incur hadd), and (c) the victim is muhsin at the time of hadd execution.
These conditions apply to all qadhf cases, including liwat under the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : رجل قال لغيره يا لوطي لا حد عليه، ولو نسبه إلى اللواطة صريحاً لا حد عليه في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال صاحباه يحد .اهـ. واعلم أنه يشترط وجود الإحصان وقت الحد حتى لو زنى المقذوف قبل أن يقام الحد على القاذف أوطئ وطئاً حراماً على ما ذكرنا أو ارتد والعياذ بالله تعالى سقط الحد عن القاذف، ولو أسلم بعد ذلك لأن إحصان المقذوف شرط فلا بد من وجوده عند إقامة الحد؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وقيد بطلبه لأنه حقه وينتفع به على الخصوص من حيث دفع العار على نفسه وإن كان الغالب فيه حق الله تعالى على الأصح. وأشار به إلى أن قذف الأخرس لا يوجب الحد لأن طلبه يكون بالإشارة ولعله لو كان ينطق لصدقه ولما كان الطلب، ثم الحد لدفع العار استفيد منه أنه لا بد من تصور الزنا من المقذوف حتى لو قذف رتقاء أو مجبوباً لا يجب عليه الحد لأنهما لا يلحقهما العار بذلك لظهور كذبه بيقين .
And in al-Khaniyyah: A man said to another 'O loti (sodomite)' — there is no hadd upon him. And if he explicitly accuses him of liwat (sodomy), there is no hadd upon him according to Abu Hanifa. And his two companions said: he incurs hadd. End quote. And know that it is required that the condition of ihsan exist at the time of the hadd. So if the accused commits zina before the hadd is carried out on the accuser, or commits unlawful intercourse, or apostatizes (may Allah protect us), the hadd is dropped from the accuser, even if he later accepts Islam, because the ihsan of the accused is a condition, so it must be present at the time of carrying out the hadd; as stated in Fath al-Qadir. And it is restricted by his demand (talab) because it is his right and he benefits from it particularly in terms of removing disgrace from himself, although it is predominantly the right of Allah on the correct view. And he indicated by this that the accusation of a mute does not necessitate the hadd because his demand would be by gesture, and perhaps if he could speak he would have confirmed him, and there would be no demand. Then the hadd is to remove disgrace, so it is understood that it is necessary that zina be conceivable from the accused. Therefore, if one accuses a woman with a closed vagina (ratqa') or a man without genitals (majbub), the hadd is not obligatory upon the accuser because they are not affected by disgrace due to the manifest falsity of his accusation.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage addresses two important issues in the law of qadhf. First, it presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding accusing someone of liwat (sodomy). According to al-Khaniyyah, if a man simply calls another 'ya loti' or explicitly accuses him of liwat, Abu Hanifa holds that the hadd of qadhf is not incurred. The reason is that the word 'zina' is not explicitly mentioned, and liwat is considered a separate act not equivalent to zina for the purpose of qadhf. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that hadd is incurred because the accusation implies a form of unlawful sexual intercourse. Second, the passage discusses the condition that the hadd is established only if the victim demands it (talab), because it is primarily his right to clear his name. Thus, if the victim is mute and cannot demand properly, no hadd. Additionally, the hadd is only imposed if the victim is capable of performing zina in a way that would bring disgrace. Therefore, accusing a woman who has a closed vagina (ratqa') or a man without genitalia (majbub) does not incur hadd, because the impossibility of zina makes the accusation clearly false and thus not defamatory. This lesson also reminds us that the condition of ihsan must be present at the time of executing the hadd; if the victim loses ihsan before the hadd is carried out (e.g., by committing zina or apostasy), the hadd is dropped.

Key Terms
لوطي (loti): A term meaning 'sodomite', used as an insult or accusation of liwat (sodomy).
اللواطة (al-liwatah): The act of sodomy (anal intercourse between men).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone explicitly accuses another of liwat (sodomy), does the hadd of qadhf apply?
A) Yes, because it is a form of zina
B) No, because liwat is not considered zina for qadhf purposes
C) Yes, because the accuser must be truthful
D) No, because the victim is not muhsin

Key Takeaway
Accusing someone of liwat does not incur the hadd of qadhf according to Abu Hanifa, because the Qur'anic text specifies zina, not liwat.

Removal of Clothes During Hadd al-Qadhf: Only Fur and Hashw Removed
Explaining the ruling on removing clothes during hadd al-qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on which clothes are removed during hadd al-qadhf and explain the istihsan reasoning based on the doubt of truthfulness.

Core Idea
During hadd al-qadhf, only fur and quilted garments are removed because the accuser might be truthful.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a unique leniency in the execution of hadd al-qadhf. Unlike other hudud punishments where the culprit is stripped almost naked, here only two specific garments—the fur coat and the padded garment—are removed. The reason lies in the inherent doubt of the accusation, which warrants a milder application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the execution of hadd al-qadhf. The ruling is that only the farw and hashw are removed; other clothes remain.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan based on the possibility that the accuser is truthful (ihtimal sidqi al-qadhif). This doubt lessens the severity.
Qiyas would have demanded full stripping, but istihsan overrides.
3
Contrast with other hudud
For hadd al-zina and hadd al-shurb, all clothes except the izar are removed. Compare the reasoning.
In those hudud, the cause (zina/drinking) is certain, so severity is applied.
4
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The fur and hashw prevent pain from reaching, so they are removed to allow the punishment to be felt, but other clothes are kept as a sign of leniency.
The removal of cushioning garments ensures the hadd is effective, while keeping other clothes shows leniency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا ينزع عنه غير الفرو والحشو إظهاراً للتخفيف لأن سببه غير متيقن به لاحتمال صدق القاذف فلا يقام على الشدة، وأما الفرو والحشو فيمنعان وصول الألم فينزعان بخلاف حد الزنا والشرب فإنه ينزع عنه ثيابه كلها إلا الإزار كما قدمناه.
His statement: (He is not stripped except of the fur and the quilted garment), as a display of leniency because its cause is not certain due to the possibility that the accuser is truthful, so it is not carried out with severity. As for the fur and the quilted garment, they prevent the pain from reaching, so they are removed, unlike the hadd for zina and drinking, where all his clothes are removed except the waist-wrapper, as we have already mentioned.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of removing clothes during the hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation of zina). The author states that during the execution of the hadd for qadhf, the culprit is not stripped of all his clothes; only the fur (fur garment) and hashw (quilted garment) are removed. The reason is that the cause of the hadd is not certain because there is a possibility that the accuser (qadhif) may be truthful—after all, the act of zina may indeed have occurred. Therefore, the punishment is carried out with leniency, not severity, by only removing these two items of clothing. In contrast, during the hadd for zina or drinking alcohol, all clothes are removed except the waist-wrapper (izar) to maximise the deterrent effect. This shows that the nature of qadhf is treated differently due to the inherent doubt regarding the truthfulness of the accusation.

Key Terms
الفرو (al-farw): A garment made of fur that covers the body and prevents the pain of the whip from reaching the skin.
الحشو (al-hashw): A quilted or stuffed garment that likewise cushions the blows. It is removed along with the fur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are only the fur and hashw removed during the hadd for qadhf?
A) Because the qadhif is wealthy and deserves mild treatment
B) Because there is a possibility that the accuser may be truthful, so the punishment is lightened
C) Because the fur and hashw are the only clothes that hinder the whip
D) Because the hadd for qadhf is a fixed punishment with no variations

Key Takeaway
In hadd al-qadhf, only the farw and hashw are removed because the accuser's truthfulness is possible, reflecting the Hanafi principle of dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat (avert hudud by doubts).

Conditions of Ihsan for Qadhf: The Four Requirements
Defining ihsan and its conditions for the hadd of qadhf to be imposed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions of ihsan for the victim of qadhf and apply them to determine whether the accuser faces hadd or ta'zir.

Core Idea
Hadd of qadhf only applies if the victim is mukallaf, free, Muslim, and chaste.

In the Hanafi school, the hadd punishment for false accusation of zina (qadhf) is not automatic on the accuser. It depends on the victim possessing a specific legal quality called ihsan. This lesson unpacks the four conditions of ihsan as defined in the classical Hanafi texts, along with their textual proofs and practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal concept of ihsan
Recognise that ihsan is a compound condition comprising four specific elements: being mukallaf, free, Muslim, and chaste. The passage defines it explicitly.
2
Derive each condition from the sources
For each condition, locate the textual evidence (Quranic verses or hadith) cited in the passage. Note how the texts prove the exclusion of minors, slaves, disbelievers, and the unchaste.
The Quranic evidence for freedom is from 4:25; the hadith for disbelief is 'man ashraka billahi falaysa bi-muhsin'; the evidence for chastity is from 5:5 and the concept of legal responsibility.
3
Apply the conditions to distinguish cases
Given a scenario, determine whether the victim has ihsan. If any condition is missing, the accuser is not liable for hadd but receives ta'zir. Practice by considering a minor, a slave, a non-Muslim, or an unchaste person.
4
Note procedural nuances and special cases
Understand how ihsan is proven in court (testimony, judge's knowledge) and consider special rules when the accuser changes his statement or when the victim is the accuser's wife (li'an).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإحصانه بكونه مكلفاً حراً مسلماً عفيفاً عن (الزنا فخرج الصبي والمجنون لأنه لا يتصور منهما الزنا إذ هو فعل محرم والحرمة بالتكليف وفي الظهيرية : إذا قذف غلاماً مراهقاً فادعى الغلام البلوغ بالسن أو الاحتلام لم يجد القاذف بقوله وخرج العبد لأن الإحصان ينتظم الحرية قال تعالى فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب [النساء : ٢٥] فقذف العبد ولو مدبراً أو مكاتباً : التعزير على قاذفه لا الحد. وخرج الكافر لقوله عليه السلام من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن». وفي الخانية : ولا يجب حد القذف إلا أن يكون المقذوف حراً ثبت حريته بإقرار القاذف أو بالبينة إذا أنكر القاذف حريته وكذا لو أنكر القاذف حرية نفسه وقال أنا عبد وعلى حد العبيد كان القول قوله اهـ. ويثبت الإحصان بشهادة رجل وامرأتين وبعلم القاضي، ولا يحلف القاذف أنه لا يعلم أن المقذوف محصن ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : لو قال لامرأته زنيت وأنت كافرة وهي في الحال مسلمة فإنه يجب اللعان وكذلك لو قال زنيت وهي أمة وهي في الحال حرة لأنه لو قال ذلك للأجنبية يجب الحد ، وهذا بخلاف ما لو قال قذفتك وأنت كافرة أو وأنت أمة .اهـ. وخرج غير العفيف لأن الإحصان ينتظم العفة أيضاً قال تعالى والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب [المائدة : ] أي العفائف ولأن المقذوف إذا لم يكن إلا أنه قد يقال يمكن تحققه منه بأن يأتي غيره ويأتيه غيره
And his being muhsin (protected from the hadd) is by his being legally responsible (mukallaf), free, Muslim, and chaste from zina. So the minor and the insane are excluded because zina is not conceivable from them, for it is a forbidden act and prohibition depends on legal responsibility. In al-Zahiriyyah: If one accuses a boy who has nearly reached puberty, and the boy claims puberty by age or nocturnal emission, the accuser is not benefited by his statement. And the slave is excluded because ihsan encompasses freedom; Allah said: 'then on them (female slaves) is half of what is upon the free women of the punishment' [al-Nisa 4:25]. So the accusation of a slave, even if he is a mudabbar or mukatib, results in ta'zir for the accuser, not hadd. And the disbeliever is excluded because the Prophet said: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not a muhsin.' In al-Khaniyyah: The hadd of qadhf is not obligatory unless the accused is free, his freedom being established by the accuser's admission or by evidence if the accuser denies his freedom. Similarly, if the accuser denies his own freedom and says 'I am a slave' and [is punished] by the hadd of slaves, his statement is accepted. And ihsan is established by the testimony of one man and two women and by the knowledge of the judge, and the accuser is not made to swear that he does not know the accused is muhsin. In al-Zahiriyyah: If a man says to his wife 'You committed zina while you were a disbeliever' and she is presently a Muslim, then the li'an ( mutual cursing) is required. Similarly, if he says 'You committed zina while you were a slave' and she is presently free, because if he said that to an unrelated woman, the hadd would be obligatory. This is contrary to if he said 'I accuse you while you were a disbeliever' or 'while you were a slave.' And the unchaste person is excluded because ihsan encompasses chastity as well; Allah said: 'And the muhsanat from among those who were given the Book' [al-Ma'idah] meaning chaste women. And because if the accused is not chaste, then it may be said that zina could have occurred from him, so the accusation is not clearly false.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the condition of ihsan for the victim in the crime of qadhf. The author defines ihsan as the victim being mukallaf (adult and sane), free, Muslim, and chaste (not having committed zina). Each condition is derived from textual evidence. For minors and the insane, zina is not legally conceivable because they lack legal responsibility. For slaves, ihsan requires freedom as per Quran 4:25, which halves the punishment for slave women. Thus, accusing a slave results only in ta'zir, not hadd. For disbelievers, the hadith 'man ashraka billahi falaysa bi-muhsin' prevents them from being considered muhsin. The passage also discusses procedural matters: establishing the freedom of the accused, proving ihsan through testimony, and exceptions when the accuser changes his statement or accuses his wife. The overarching principle is that the hadd of qadhf is not established unless the victim is muhsin in all these aspects at the time of the hadd.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The quality of being muhsin: legally responsible, free, Muslim, and chaste from zina, which protects the accused from the hadd of qadhf.
محصن (muhsin): A person who possesses ihsan: mukallaf, free, Muslim, and chaste.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the victim to be muhsin in qadhf?
A) Being mukallaf (adult and sane)
B) Being free
C) Being Muslim
D) Being wealthy

Key Takeaway
The hadd for qadhf is only established when the victim possesses all four conditions of ihsan: legal capacity, freedom, Islam, and chastity.

Removal of Clothes in Hadd Qadhf
Ruling on what garments are removed when executing hadd for false accusation of zina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which garments are removed during hadd qadhf according to the Hanafi school and explain the reasoning of leniency due to uncertainty of guilt.

Core Idea
Leniency in hadd qadhf: only fur and quilted garments removed because the accusation may be true.

The execution of hadd for false accusation of zina (qadhf) is unique in the Hanafi school. Unlike other hudud punishments, the procedure here is deliberately lenient. Why? Because the very cause of the punishment—the accusation—might be truthful. This lesson unpacks exactly which garments are removed and the legal reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the punishment and its cause
Recognize that the punishment is hadd for qadhf (false accusation of zina). Its cause is the accusation itself, but the certainty of guilt is undermined by the possibility of the accuser being truthful.
This uncertainty is the key to the whole ruling.
2
State the general rule of garment removal
Note that only the farw (fur garment) and hushw (quilted garment) are removed. All other clothes remain on the condemned person.
This contrasts with hadd for zina and shurb where all clothes except the wrapper are removed.
3
Explain the reasoning (ta'lil)
The underlying principle is istihsan (juristic preference) for leniency because the sabab (cause) of the punishment is not certain (ghayr mutayaqqin). Removing only bulky garments that block pain avoids unnecessary severity.
The fur and quilted garments are removed precisely because they prevent the pain of the lashes from reaching the body.
4
Clarify the definition of hushw
Hushw refers specifically to a garment that is stuffed with cotton or similar material (mahshew). A simple lined garment (with batinah) without stuffing is not removed.
This distinction is derived from the implication of the scholars' statements.
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi nuance about the shirt
According to Fath al-Qadir, if the person is wearing a shirt (qamees) over the hushw, the shirt is also removed because it becomes like a quilted garment and would block pain.
This shows that the operative principle is prevention of pain, not the garment type alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا ينزع عنه غير الفرو والحشو إظهاراً للتخفيف لأن سببه غير متيقن به لاحتمال صدق القاذف فلا يقام على الشدة، وأما الفرو والحشو فيمنعان وصول الألم فينزعان بخلاف حد الزنا والشرب فإنه ينزع عنه ثيابه كلها إلا الإزار كما قدمناه. والمراد بالحشو الثوب المحشو كالمضرب بالقطن ومقتضى كلامهم أنه لو كان عليه ثوب ذو بطانة غير محشو لا ينزع. وفي فتح القدير والظاهر أنه لو كان فوق قميص ينزع لأنه القميص يصير مع كالمحشو أو قريباً منه ويمنع من إيصال الألم الذي يصلح زاجراً
He said: (And nothing is removed from him except the fur and the quilted garment) as a manifestation of leniency, because its cause is not certain due to the possibility of the accuser being truthful, so it is not carried out with severity. As for the fur and the quilted garment, they prevent the arrival of pain, so they are removed, unlike the hadd of zina and drinking, for which all his clothes are removed except the wrapper, as we have mentioned before. And by al-hushw is meant the quilted garment, like a cotton-filled blanket. And the implication of their statement is that if he had a garment with a lining that is not quilted, it is not removed. And in Fath al-Qadir: The apparent view is that if there is a shirt over it, it is removed, because the shirt becomes like a quilted garment or close to it, and it prevents the delivery of pain that would serve as a deterrent.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the execution of the hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation of zina). The Hanafi school holds that because the cause of the punishment (the accusation) is not certain—since the accuser might be truthful—the punishment is carried out with leniency. Therefore, only the fur garment (farrow) and the quilted garment (hushw) are removed, as they block the pain of the lashes. However, all other clothes are left on, unlike the hadd for zina and drinking wine, where all clothes except a wrapper (izar) are removed. The text then clarifies that al-hushw refers to a garment stuffed with cotton or similar material. If a garment has a lining but is not quilted, it is not removed according to the implication of the scholars' statements. But in Fath al-Qadir, it is stated that if the person has a shirt over the quilted garment, the shirt is also removed because it becomes like a quilted garment and would prevent the pain from reaching the skin effectively.

Key Terms
فرو (farw): A fur garment worn for warmth.
حشو (hushw): A quilted garment stuffed with cotton or similar material.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why are only the fur and quilted garments removed during the execution of hadd for qadhf?
A) Because these are the most painful garments.
B) Because the cause of punishment is certain.
C) Because the cause is uncertain (possible truthfulness), so severity is avoided.
D) Because the Prophet (PBUH) specified it.

Key Takeaway
Hadd qadhf is executed leniently by removing only garments that block pain, due to the uncertainty of the guilt.

Conditions of Ihsan for Hadd Qadhf
Definition and elaboration of ihsan conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan for hadd qadhf and identify which condition is missing in a given scenario.

Core Idea
A qazif only receives hadd if the accused is muhsan: mukallaf, free, Muslim, and chaste from zina.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the legal status of being muhsan in the context of hadd al-qadhf. The Hanafi school specifies five conditions that the accused must meet for the accuser to be liable for the fixed punishment of 80 lashes. If any condition is absent, the punishment reduces to ta'zir. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying this hudud ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Locate the phrase 'wa ihsanuhu bi kawnihi mukallafan hurran musliman afifan 'an al-zina' in the Arabic text. This is the core definition listing the five conditions.
2
Examine each condition's rationale
For each condition (mukallaf, free, Muslim, chaste from zina), read the commentary explaining why it is excluded if missing. Note the Quranic and hadith evidence provided.
The text uses Quran 4:25 for freedom and hadith for disbelief.
3
Understand the consequence of missing a condition
The text repeatedly states that if any condition is absent, the accuser receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment) instead of hadd. Confirm this from the passage.
4
Apply to specific cases
Work through the subsidiary cases mentioned: qadhf of a slave, a disbeliever, a non-chaste person, a minor, or an insane person. Determine the punishment for the accuser in each.
5
Analyse the temporal nuance
Consider the case where the accuser says 'you committed zina while you were a disbeliever/slave' and the accused is currently Muslim/free. The passage explains that the relevant moment is the time of accusation, not the time of the alleged act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإحصانه بكونه مكلفاً حراً مسلماً عفيفاً عن (الزنا فخرج الصبي والمجنون لأنه لا يتصور منهما الزنا إذ هو فعل محرم والحرمة بالتكليف وفي الظهيرية : إذا قذف غلاماً مراهقاً فادعى الغلام البلوغ بالسن أو الاحتلام لم يجد القاذف بقوله وخرج العبد لأن الإحصان ينتظم الحرية قال تعالى فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب [النساء : ٢٥] فقذف العبد ولو مدبراً أو مكاتباً : التعزير على قاذفه لا الحد. وخرج الكافر لقوله عليه السلام من أشرك بالله فليس بمحصن». وفي الخانية : ولا يجب حد القذف إلا أن يكون المقذوف حراً ثبت حريته بإقرار القاذف أو بالبينة إذا أنكر القاذف حريته وكذا لو أنكر القاذف حرية نفسه وقال أنا عبد وعلى حد العبيد كان القول قوله اهـ. ويثبت الإحصان بشهادة رجل وامرأتين وبعلم القاضي، ولا يحلف القاذف أنه لا يعلم أن المقذوف محصن ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : لو قال لامرأته زنيت وأنت كافرة وهي في الحال مسلمة فإنه يجب اللعان وكذلك لو قال زنيت وهي أمة وهي في الحال حرة لأنه لو قال ذلك للأجنبية يجب الحد ، وهذا بخلاف ما لو قال قذفتك وأنت كافرة أو وأنت أمة .اهـ. وخرج غير العفيف لأن الإحصان ينتظم العفة أيضاً قال تعالى والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب [المائدة : ] أي العفائف ولأن المقذوف إذا لم يكن إلا أنه قد يقال يمكن تحققه منه بأن يأتي غيره ويأتيه غيره وعبارة السراجية مطلقة وهي على ما في التتارخانية قذف خنثى بلغ مشكلاً ولم يتبين حاله لم يحد فتأمل. ثم ظهر لي أن مراد النهر حمل المسألة على ما إذا تزوج الخنثى المذكور ودخل فقذفه آخر فإنه لا يحد بقذفه لأنه وطئ في غير ملكه لكون نكاحه موقوفاً لا يفيد الحل فلا يرد عليه ما مر أصلاً قوله : (لم يحد القاذف بقوله) قال في الشرنبلالية : فهذا يستثنى من قول أئمتنا لو راهقا وقالا بلغنا صدقاً وأحكامهما أحكام البالغين. قوله : (وفي الظهيرية لو قال لامرأته زنيت وأنت كافرة الخ قال المؤلف في باب اللعان نقلاً عن الفتح : ولو أسند الزنا بأن قال زنيت وأنت صبية أو مجنونة وهو معهود وهي الآن أهل فلا لعان بخلاف وأنت ذمية أو أمة أو منذ أربعين سنة وعمرها أقل تلاعناً لاقتصاره قوله : (لأنه لو قال ذلك للأجنبية يجب الحد لأنه قاذف يوم تكلم بزناها والمعتبر عندنا في القذف حال ظهوره دون حال الإضافة ؛ كذا في الجوهرة. قال في منح الغفار أقول ما ذكره من الأصل مشكل لأنه إن اعتبر في عفيفاً فالقاذف صادق فالشرائط الخمسة للإحصان داخلة تحت قوله تعالى والذين يرمون المحصنات [النور: ٤] فإذا فقد واحد منها لا يكون محصناً. وفي القنية : قذف وهو مصلح ظاهراً ولم يكن عفيفاً في السر يعذر في مطالبة القاذف بالحد فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى. قال رضي الله عنه : فيه نظر فإن المفهوم من قوله ولم يكن عفيفاً في السر أنه من الزنا وإن كان زانياً لم يكن قذفه موجباً للحد فكيف يعذر؟ اهـ . وقيد بقوله عن الزنا» لأنه لا يشترط العفة عن الوطء الحرام
He said: (And his being muhsan is by him being legally responsible, free, Muslim, chaste from zina). So the minor and the insane are excluded, because zina cannot be conceived from them, as it is a forbidden act and prohibition is based on legal responsibility. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he accuses a mature minor boy and the boy claims puberty by age or nocturnal emission, the accuser's statement does not avail him. And the slave is excluded because ihsan requires freedom, Allah says: '...then for them half of what is prescribed for muhsanat women' [al-Nisa' 4:25]. So qadhf of a slave, even a mudabbar or mukatab, requires ta'zir for the accuser, not hadd. And the disbeliever is excluded because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' And in al-Khaniyyah: hadd qadhf is not obligatory unless the accused is free, his freedom being established by the accuser's admission or by evidence if the accuser denies his freedom. Likewise, if the accuser denies his own freedom and says 'I am a slave and subject to the hadd of slaves,' his statement is accepted. And ihsan is established by the testimony of one man and two women and by the knowledge of the judge, and the accuser is not made to take an oath that he does not know the accused is muhsan; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he says to his wife 'You committed zina while you were a disbeliever' and she is currently Muslim, then li'an is obligatory; likewise if he says 'you committed zina while you were a slave' and she is currently free, because if he said that to a stranger, hadd would be obligatory. This differs from if he said 'I accuse you of zina while you were a disbeliever' or 'while you were a slave'. And the non-chaste is excluded because ihsan also includes chastity, Allah says: 'And muhsanat from those who were given the Book' [al-Ma'idah], meaning chaste women. And because the accused if not... (remainder omitted for brevity) ...He restricted it by his saying 'from zina' because chastity from unlawful intercourse other than zina is not required.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a definition and elaboration of the conditions for a person to be considered muhsan (in a state that makes the accuser liable for hadd). The Hanafi school stipulates five conditions: the accused must be (1) legally responsible (mukallaf: adult and sane), (2) free, (3) Muslim, (4) chaste from zina. If any condition is missing, the accuser receives ta'zir instead of hadd. The text provides detailed rulings for each exclusion: minors and the insane cannot commit zina conceptually; slaves and disbelievers are excluded by Quran and Hadith; and the non-chaste (someone who has committed zina) is excluded because ihsan includes chastity. The passage also discusses subsidiary issues: how freedom is proven, the establishment of ihsan by testimony or judicial knowledge, and the case of a khuntha (hermaphrodite) whose status is ambiguous. It also addresses the situation where the accuser says 'you committed zina while you were a disbeliever/slave' and the accused is currently Muslim/free—the ruling depends on the state at the time of accusation. The author then comments on the condition of chastity, noting that only chastity from zina (not other unlawful intercourse) is required, and discusses the case of a person who appears chaste but is secretly an adulterer.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): In the context of qadhf, a legal status requiring five conditions: being legally responsible, free, Muslim, and chaste from zina.
محصن (muhsan): A person who fulfills the five conditions of ihsan, making the accuser liable for hadd.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment less than hadd, imposed when conditions for hadd are not fully met.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT one of the conditions for a person to be considered muhsan in the context of hadd qadhf?
A) Being legally responsible (mukallaf).
B) Being free.
C) Being married.
D) Being chaste from zina.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ihsan for hadd qadhf through five specific conditions; absence of any one reduces the punishment to ta'zir.

Cases Where Wati' is Not Zina: Effect on Hadd Qadhf
Rulings on when wati' is not zina and effect on hadd qadhf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify specific cases of sexual intercourse that are not legally classified as zina in the Hanafi school and explain why qadhf against such persons does not incur the hadd punishment.

Core Idea
Hadd qadhf only applies when the alleged act is legally zina; intercourse by ownership or shubha is not zina.

In Hanafi criminal law, the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf) is a severe penalty reserved for accusing someone of zina. However, the definition of zina is precise. This lesson, drawn from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, presents multiple scenarios where sexual intercourse occurs but is not considered zina, such as with one's own slave-girl or under a mistaken belief of legality. Understanding these exceptions is crucial to properly applying the law of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific case
Read the passage and list the different scenarios mentioned. For each, note the nature of the intercourse (e.g., with own slave-girl, with a slave-girl in her 'idda, with a woman believed to be lawful).
2
Determine legal status of the intercourse
For each case, assess whether the intercourse is considered zina in Hanafi law. Look for the reason: is it ownership, valid marriage, shubha, or something else? The key is whether the act is legally defined as zina.
3
Apply the rule on qadhf
If the intercourse is not zina, then accusing a person of zina in that context does not constitute qadhf that incurs hadd. The accuser may still be liable for ta'zir (discretionary punishment) but not the fixed hadd penalty.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text points to a difference of opinion, e.g., regarding intercourse with a son's slave-girl. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ from Abu Hanifa on some details. Understand the nuance and the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لذا قال في الظهيرية لو وطئ أمته المرتدة حد قاذفه ولو تزوج أمة على حرة فوطئها فإني أحد قاذفه ; كذا في المنتقى عن أبي يوسف قال الحاكم أبو الفضل : هذا خلاف ما في الأصل قال : ثم كل شيء اختلف فيه الفقهاء حرمه بعضهم وأحله بعضهم فإني أحد قاذفه . صحيح، وفيه أيضاً: لو وطئ أمته في عدة من زوج لها فإني أحد قاذفه لأن ملكه في أمته , ولو وطىء جارية ابنه في عدة من زوج لها فأحبلها أو لم يحبلها فإنه يحد قاذفه. قال أبو يوسف : كل من درأت الحد عنه وجعلت عليه المهر وأثبت نسب الولد منه فإني أحد قاذفه، وكذلك لو تزوج أمة لرجل بغير إذنه ودخل بها فإني أحد قاذفه. هشام عن محمد في رجل اشترى أمة فوطئها ثم استبان أنها أخته حد قاذفه ابن سماعة عن محمد في الرقيات : أربعة شهدوا على رجل أنه زنى بفلانة بنت فلان الفلانية امرأة معروفة سموها ووصفوا الزنا فأثبتوه والمرأة غائبة فرجم الرجل، ثم إن رجلاً قذف تلك المرأة الغائبة فخاصمته إلى القاضي القذف حال ظهوره دون حال الإضافة لزم أن يحد في قوله زنيت بك وأنت صغيرة، وكذا في نظائره فليتأمل .اهـ. وأجاب الرملي في حاشيته عليه بأنه في الصغيرة ليس بقذف لعدم تصوره منها إذ ذاك ولذا لم يسقط به إحصانها بخلاف الأمة والكافرة فيحد لتصوره ولذلك يسقط الإحصان فلم يدخل الأول في الأصل اهـ. وإلى هذا أشار في الفتح حيث قال : ولو قال زنيت وأنت صغيرة لم يحد لعدم الإثم. قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه فيه نظر الخ قال في النهر : يؤيده أن رفع العار مجوز لا ملزم وإلا لامتنع عفوه عنه وأجبر على الدعوى وهو خلاف الواقع .اهـ. قلت بل قال في التتارخانية عن تجنيس الناصري : وحسن أن لا يرفع القاذف إلى القاضي ولا يطالبه بالحد، وحسن من الإمام أن يقول للمقذوف قبل أن يثبت عليه الحد أعرض عن هذا أودعه .اهـ. قوله : (لأنه لا تشترط العفة عن الوطء الحرام) نظر فيه بأن من جملة الوطء الحرام الذي ليس بزنا الوطء بنكاح فاسد والوطء بشبهة مع ا أنه تشترط العفة عنهما . وأجيب بأنه أراد الحرام لغيره والقرينة عليه ما يأتي آخر المقولة عن شرح الطحاوي، وكذا ما يأتي عند قول المتن ومن قذف امرأة لم يدر أبو ولدها الخ فراجعه فإنه صريح في ذلك . قوله : (ولو وطئ جارية ابنه في عدة من زوج لها الخ أقول : قدم أول كتاب الحدود أنه لو وطئ جارية ابنه لا يحد للزنا ولا يحد قاذفه بالزنا. وصرح به في الفتح أيضاً أول باب الوطء الذي لا يوجب الحد. وسيأتي أيضاً عند قول المصنف فيمن لا يحد قاذفه أو وطئ في غير ملكه أنه دخل فيه جارية ابنه»
(Complete translation omitted due to length, but key points: The text discusses various scenarios where sexual intercourse does not count as zina, so qadhf does not incur hadd. Examples: having intercourse with one's own apostate slave-girl, marrying a slave-girl over a free woman, etc. The principle is that if the wati' is not considered zina (e.g., due to ownership, valid marriage, or uncertainty), then qadhf of such a person does not require hadd. The text also discusses the consideration of time: the ruling on qadhf is based on the status at the time of accusation, not the time of the alleged act. The author comments on the condition of chastity and various exceptions.)
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on when certain types of sexual intercourse are not considered zina, and consequently, accusing someone of zina in these contexts does not incur the hadd punishment for qadhf. The examples include: having intercourse with one's own apostate slave-girl (since ownership continues despite apostasy), marrying a slave-girl while already married to a free woman (the marriage is valid but may be considered makruh or haram, but not zina), having intercourse with a slave-girl during her 'idda from a previous husband (since ownership is established, it is not zina), and a case where a man purchases a slave-girl and has intercourse with her only to discover she is his sister (the intercourse is with shubha, not zina). These cases illustrate the broader principle that qadhf is only for actual zina, not for intercourse that is permissible or dhawa. The text also revisits the principle that the time of the accusation governs, not the time of the alleged act, and discusses the case of accusing a minor (which is not zina and thus no hadd). The author includes comments from later scholars like al-Ramli and references from Fath al-Qadir and al-Nahr.

Key Terms
وطء بشبهة (wat' bi-shubha): Sexual intercourse under a mistaken belief of legality (e.g., ownership or marriage).
مهر (mahr): Dower; in some cases, if wati' is not zina, mahr is obligatory but hadd is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man has intercourse with his own female slave, and someone accuses him of zina, what is the ruling?
A) The accuser is flogged with hadd.
B) The accuser is not punished at all.
C) The man is flogged for zina.
D) The slave-girl is flogged.

Key Takeaway
Hadd qadhf is only incurred when the alleged act is legally zina; many forms of unlawful or doubtful intercourse are not considered zina, thus protecting the accuser from hadd.

The Five Conditions of Ihsan for Qadhf
Defines the five conditions of ihsan and addresses cases of apparent chastity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan for hadd al-qadhf and apply them to determine whether the accused is liable for hadd or ta'zir.

Core Idea
A valid qadhf requires a muhsan victim; without all five conditions, no hadd.

In this passage, the author opens the chapter on qadhf by establishing the foundational rule: the victim must be muhsan (chaste). The five conditions of ihsan are derived from the Quranic verse 24:4. The passage then examines borderline cases, such as when the victim secretly commits zina or makes an inconceivable accusation. Understanding these conditions is essential to correctly applying the hadd of qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central condition
The passage states that qadhf requires the victim to be muhsan. List the five implied conditions: adulthood, sanity, freedom, Islam, and freedom from zina (actual chastity).
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 24:4 is cited: 'And those who accuse chaste women (muhsanat).' The word 'muhsanat' indicates the conditions of ihsan.
The verse is qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala; the Hanafi school interprets it as requiring actual chastity.
3
Analyze the problematic case
The text discusses a person who appears righteous but is not chaste in secret. The author criticizes the notion that such a person is excused from demanding hadd, because if he is actually an adulterer, the accuser is not guilty of qadhf.
The resolution is that the condition is freedom from zina, not from all forbidden intercourse.
4
Work through the examples
Examine the scenarios: wati' of a murtadda slave-girl, marrying a slave-girl while having a free wife, wati' of one's own slave-girl in idda, wati' of a son's slave-girl, and saying 'I committed zina with you when you were a child.' Determine when hadd applies.
Abu Yusuf's general rule: anyone for whom hadd for zina is waived but mahr and lineage are established, the accuser is subject to hadd.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Compare the Hanafi requirement of actual chastity with the Shafi'i view that apparent chastity suffices. The passage implicitly supports the Hanafi position.
This difference affects cases where the victim secretly commits zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود/ باب حد القذف عفيفاً فالقاذف صادق فالشرائط الخمسة للإحصان داخلة تحت قوله تعالى والذين يرمون المحصنات [النور: ٤] فإذا فقد واحد منها لا يكون محصناً. وفي القنية : قذف وهو مصلح ظاهراً ولم يكن عفيفاً في السر يعذر في مطالبة القاذف بالحد فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى. قال رضي الله عنه : فيه نظر فإن المفهوم من قوله ولم يكن عفيفاً في السر أنه من الزنا وإن كان زانياً لم يكن قذفه موجباً للحد فكيف يعذر؟ اهـ . وقيد بقوله عن الزنا» لأنه لا يشترط العفة عن الوطء الحرام ولذا قال في الظهيرية لو وطئ أمته المرتدة حد قاذفه ولو تزوج أمة على حرة فوطئها فإني أحد قاذفه ؛ كذا في المنتقى عن أبي يوسف قال الحاكم أبو الفضل : هذا خلاف ما في الأصل قال : ثم كل شيء اختلف فيه الفقهاء حرمه بعضهم وأحله بعضهم فإني أحد قاذفه . صحيح، وفيه أيضاً: لو وطئ أمته في عدة من زوج لها فإني أحد قاذفه لأن ملكه في أمته ، ولو وطىء جارية ابنه في عدة من زوج لها فأحبلها أو لم يحبلها فإنه يحد قاذفه. قال أبو يوسف : كل من درأت الحد عنه وجعلت عليه المهر وأثبت نسب الولد منه فإني أحد قاذفه، وكذلك لو تزوج أمة لرجل بغير إذنه ودخل بها فإني أحد قاذفه. هشام عن محمد في رجل اشترى أمة فوطئها ثم استبان أنها أخته حد قاذفه ابن سماعة عن محمد في الرقيات : أربعة شهدوا على رجل أنه زنى بفلانة بنت فلان الفلانية امرأة معروفة سموها ووصفوا الزنا فأثبتوه والمرأة غائبة فرجم الرجل، ثم إن رجلاً قذف تلك المرأة الغائبة فخاصمته إلى القاضي القذف حال ظهوره دون حال الإضافة لزم أن يحد في قوله زنيت بك وأنت صغيرة، وكذا في نظائره فليتأمل .اهـ. وأجاب الرملي في حاشيته عليه بأنه في الصغيرة ليس بقذف لعدم تصوره منها إذ ذاك ولذا لم يسقط به إحصانها بخلاف الأمة والكافرة فيحد لتصوره ولذلك يسقط الإحصان فلم يدخل الأول في الأصل اهـ. وإلى هذا أشار في الفتح حيث قال : ولو قال زنيت وأنت صغيرة لم يحد لعدم الإثم.
The Book of Hudud / Chapter of Qadhf. [The victim must be] chaste, so the accuser is truthful. Thus the five conditions of ihsan are included under His statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women' [an-Nur:4]. If one condition is absent, she is not muhsana. In al-Qunya: if he is an apparent reformer but not chaste in secret, he is excused from demanding the hadd from his accuser between him and Allah. He (may Allah be pleased with him) said: There is consideration in this, because what is understood from his statement 'not chaste in secret' is that he is an adulterer, and if he is an adulterer, his qadhf does not necessitate hadd, so how can he be excused? He qualified by saying 'about zina' because chastity from forbidden intercourse is not a condition. Therefore, in al-Dhahiriyya: if he wati'a his apostate slave-girl, his accuser is to be given hadd. If he married a slave-girl while having a free wife and wati'a her, I will subject his accuser to hadd. Likewise in al-Muntaqa from Abu Yusuf. Al-Hakim Abu al-Fadl said: This contradicts what is in al-Asl. He said: Then for everything about which the fuqaha differed, some making it haram and some halal, I will subject his accuser to hadd. Sahih. Also in it: if he wati'a his slave-girl during her idda from a husband, I will subject his accuser to hadd because he owns his slave-girl. And if he wati'a his son's slave-girl during her idda from a husband, and he made her pregnant or not, his accuser is to be given hadd. Abu Yusuf said: Everyone for whom I ward off the hadd, impose the mahr, and establish lineage of the child from him, I will subject his accuser to hadd. Similarly, if he married another man's slave-girl without permission and entered her, I will subject his accuser to hadd. Hisham from Muhammad: concerning a man who bought a slave-girl and wati'a her, then it became clear that she was his sister, his accuser is to be given hadd. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad in al-Ruqiyyat: four witnesses testified against a man that he committed zina with so-and-so's daughter, a known woman, naming her and describing the zina, and they established it, and the woman was absent, so the man was stoned. Then a man qadhafa that absent woman, and she brought him to the judge. [The author said:] Qadhf in the state of appearance, not in the state of attribution, necessitates that he should be given hadd for saying 'I committed zina with you when you were a child', and similarly for analogous cases; let it be pondered. Al-Ramli answered in his Hashiya that for a child, it is not qadhf because it is inconceivable from her then, so it does not remove her ihsan, unlike the slave-girl and the disbeliever, for he is given hadd because it is conceivable, and thus ihsan is removed, so the first is not included in the original. This is indicated in al-Fath where it says: If he said 'I committed zina with you when you were a child', he is not given hadd due to lack of sin.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, opening the chapter on qadhf (false accusation of zina) from the Book of Hudud. The author establishes the central condition for hadd al-qadhf: the victim must be muhsan (chaste, i.e., free, adult, Muslim, and chaste from zina). These five conditions are derived from the Quranic verse 24:4, and if any is missing, the accuser is not subject to hadd (he may be punished for slander instead). The text then discusses a problematic case from al-Qunya: a person appears righteous but commits zina in secret; the author criticizes the notion that such a person is excused from demanding hadd, because if he is actually an adulterer, the accuser is not liable (since the victim is not muhsan). The author resolves this by explaining that the condition is freedom from zina, not from all forbidden intercourse (like wati' in a fasid contract or with a slave-girl in idda). Several examples follow: wati' of a murtadda slave-girl, marrying a slave-girl while having a free wife, wati' of one's own slave-girl in her idda, and wati' of a son's slave-girl—all these do not remove ihsan for the purpose of qadhf, so the accuser is subject to hadd. Abu Yusuf gives a general rule: anyone for whom I (the judge) waive the hadd for zina but impose mahr and establish lineage, the accuser is subject to hadd. The passage then addresses a specific case: if someone says 'I committed zina with you when you were a child'—this is not qadhf because it is physically inconceivable, so the victim remains muhsan. The commentary connects this to the earlier discussion and clarifies that for a slave-girl or a disbeliever, such a statement is qadhf because zina is conceivable.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-ihsan): The state of being chaste (muhsan), which involves being free, adult, Muslim, and free from zina.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is qadhf if the victim is a slave-girl or disbeliever
D) The accuser is subject to ta'zir only

Key Takeaway
Hadd al-qadhf only applies when the victim meets all five conditions of ihsan, with actual chastity from zina being a key Hanafi requirement.

Types of Intercourse That Remove Ihsan for Qadhf
Classifies types of wati' that do or do not remove ihsan for qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between intercourse that removes ihsan and intercourse that does not, applying the Hanafi principle of milk al-mut'a, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on touching/looking with desire.

Core Idea
Ihsan is removed only by zina-like intercourse lacking full ownership of pleasure, not by temporary prohibitions.

In the law of qadhf, the hadd penalty is only obligatory if the victim is muhsan (chaste). Ihsan is lost by certain types of intercourse. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq classifies various scenarios, distinguishing between zina, wat' bi shubha, nikkah fasid, and intercourse with a perpetually prohibited relative (removing ihsan) versus intercourse during menstruation or with a Magian slave-girl (not removing ihsan). A key disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn about the effect of touching/looking with desire at the slave-girl's mahram is also presented. Follow the guided steps to work through the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Identify the overarching rule: ihsan is removed by zina in every respect (every intercourse forbidden due to lack of milk al-mut'a), but not by intercourse forbidden despite full milk al-mut'a due to a temporary impediment.
The principle is explicitly stated in the passage: 'كل وطء حرم لعدم ملك المتعة ... فهو زنا من كل وجه'.
2
Apply the principle to specific cases
Work through each case mentioned: wati' of a Magian slave-girl (not removed), wati' during menstruation (not removed), wati' of a foster-sister (removed because prohibition is perpetual). For each, identify the presence or absence of full milk al-mut'a.
The prohibition of a Magian slave-girl is due to her disbelief, which does not negate ownership; the prohibition of menstruation is temporary.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Examine the ikhtilaf when a man touches/looks with desire at the slave-girl's mahram before wati'. Abu Hanifa holds that ihsan remains; the Sahibayn hold that it is removed. Determine the basis: does the act affect milk al-mut'a or create a permanent prohibition?
Abu Hanifa views the act as not removing full ownership; the Sahibayn see it as rendering the woman like a perpetually prohibited relative.
4
Evaluate the evidence and tarjih
Consider the reasoning of both sides. The Sahibayn analogize to wati' of a foster-sister (perpetual prohibition). The passage does not give a clear tarjih; later fatwa may prefer the Sahibayn. Note the authority weight: this is from zahir al-riwayah.
The qiyas panel in the analytical toolbox shows the reasoning on a related case (Magian slave-girl) which can be compared.
5
Formulate the mufta bihi ruling
Based on the text and the note about later fatwa, state the operative position: for the touching/looking case, many later Hanafi scholars adopt the view of the Sahibayn that ihsan is removed. Confirm this with the authority from the toolbox.
The hanafi_position_box indicates mufta bihi may follow Sahibayn.

قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه فيه نظر الخ قال في النهر : يؤيده أن رفع العار مجوز لا ملزم وإلا لامتنع عفوه عنه وأجبر على الدعوى وهو خلاف الواقع .اهـ. قلت بل قال في التتارخانية عن تجنيس الناصري : وحسن أن لا يرفع القاذف إلى القاضي ولا يطالبه بالحد، وحسن من الإمام أن يقول للمقذوف قبل أن يثبت عليه الحد أعرض عن هذا أودعه .اهـ. قوله : (لأنه لا تشترط العفة عن الوطء الحرام) نظر فيه بأن من جملة الوطء الحرام الذي ليس بزنا الوطء بنكاح فاسد والوطء بشبهة مع ا أنه تشترط العفة عنهما . وأجيب بأنه أراد الحرام لغيره والقرينة عليه ما يأتي آخر المقولة عن شرح الطحاوي، وكذا ما يأتي عند قول المتن ومن قذف امرأة لم يدر أبو ولدها الخ فراجعه فإنه صريح في ذلك . قوله : (ولو وطئ جارية ابنه في عدة من زوج لها الخ أقول : قدم أول كتاب الحدود أنه لو وطئ جارية ابنه لا يحد للزنا ولا يحد قاذفه بالزنا. وصرح به في الفتح أيضاً أول باب الوطء الذي لا يوجب الحد. وسيأتي أيضاً عند قول المصنف فيمن لا يحد قاذفه أو وطئ في غير ملكه أنه دخل فيه جارية ابنه» . كتاب الحدود باب حد القذف ٥٥ لغيره لست لأبيك أو لست بابن فلان في غضب حد وفي غيره لا كنفيه عن جده الذي قضى على الرجل بالرجم قال : القياس أن يحد قاذفها لأن القاضي إنما قضى عليه لا عليها لكني أستحسن أن لا أحد قاذفها ثم قال : وكما يزول الإحصان بالزنا من كل وجه يزول بالزنا من وجه، فكل وطء حرم لعدم ملك المتعة من وجه فهو زنا من كل وجه وذلك كوطء الأجنبية، وكل وطء حرم مع قيام ملك المتعة من كل وجه لعارض كوطء المرأة في حالة الحيض لا يزول به الإحصان. وإذا وطئ أمته المجوسية لا يزول إحصانه لقيام ملك المتعة من كل وجه ولو اشترى أمة وطئها أبوه أو وطئ هو أمها ووطئها فقذفه إنسان فلا حد على القاذف بالإجماع، وكذا لو اشترى أخته من الرضاعة ووطئها سقط إحصانه لأن الحرمة هنا ثابتة على سبيل التأبيد بخلاف ما تقدم. ولو اشترى أمة لمس أمها أو بنتها بشهوة أو نظر إلى فرج أمها أو بنتها بشهوة أو نظر أبوه أو ابنه إلى فرجها بشهوة ووطئها قال أبو حنيفة : لا يزول إحصانه ويحد قاذفته :وقالا : يزول إحصانه ولا فاسد في عمره أو وطئ من هي محرمة عليه على التأبيد سقط إحصانه ومالا فلا؛ كذا في شرح الطحاوي.
His statement: (He, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'there is consideration in it'). An-Nahr said: It is supported that removing disgrace is permissible, not obligatory; otherwise, his forgiveness would be impossible and he would be forced to sue, contrary to reality. I said: Rather, in at-Tatar Khaniyya from Tajnis an-Nasiri: It is good that the accuser is not brought to the judge and not asked for the hadd, and it is good for the imam to say to the accused before establishing the hadd: 'Turn away from this or leave it.' His statement: (Because chastity from forbidden intercourse is not a condition) – it is considered that among the forbidden intercourse that is not zina is intercourse in a fasid marriage and with shubha, and yet chastity from them is a condition. The answer is that he meant the forbidden for other reasons, and the evidence is what comes at the end of the statement from Sharh at-Tahawi, and also what comes at the statement of the matn: 'Whoever qadhafa a woman whose child's father is unknown', etc., so refer to it, for it is explicit on that. His statement: (And if he wati'a his son's slave-girl in her idda from a husband, etc.) I say: It was presented at the beginning of the Book of Hudud that if he wati'a his son's slave-girl, he is not given hadd for zina, and his accuser is not given hadd for zina. This is also stated in al-Fath at the beginning of the chapter of intercourse that does not necessitate hadd. It will also come at the statement of the author regarding those whose accuser is not given hadd: 'or he wati'a outside his ownership' that it includes his son's slave-girl. The Book of Hudud, chapter of Qadhf, page 55. For other than him: 'You are not from your father' or 'You are not the son of so-and-so' in anger, he is given hadd; otherwise, no. (Continuous:) The one who ruled that the man be stoned said: Qiyas is that her accuser should be given hadd because the judge only ruled against him, not against her, but I like to not give her accuser hadd. Then he said: Just as ihsan is removed by zina entirely, it is removed by zina in one respect. So every intercourse that is forbidden due to lack of ownership of pleasure in one respect is zina entirely, like intercourse with a foreign woman. And every intercourse that is forbidden despite full ownership of pleasure due to a temporary impediment, like intercourse during menstruation, does not remove ihsan. If he wati'a his Magian slave-girl, his ihsan is not removed due to full ownership of pleasure. And if he purchased a slave-girl that his father had wati'a, or he wati'a her mother and then her, and someone qadhafa him, there is no hadd on the qadif by consensus. Similarly, if he purchased his foster-sister and wati'a her, his ihsan is removed because the prohibition here is perpetual, unlike before. And if he purchased a slave-girl and touched her mother or daughter with desire, or looked at the genitals of her mother or daughter with desire, or his father or son looked at her genitals with desire, and then he wati'a her, Abu Hanifa said: His ihsan is not removed and his accuser is given hadd. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: His ihsan is removed and his accuser is not given hadd. Similarly, there is a difference if he married a woman of this description and wati'a her. In al-Khaniyya, it is considered that whoever wati'a in a fasid marriage, like one who wati'a a joint-owned slave-girl, there is no hadd on the qadif. The conclusion: Whoever commits zina, or wati'a with shubha, or in a fasid marriage in his life, or wati'a someone perpetually prohibited to him, his ihsan is removed; otherwise, no. This is from Sharh at-Tahawi.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and expansion of the ruling on what removes ihsan. It begins by commenting on the author's earlier criticism, pointing out that the victim's right to demand hadd is not obligatory; the imam may advise forgiveness. The text then addresses a nuance: chastity is required from zina, not from all forbidden intercourse (e.g., nikkah fasid, shubha) — but then qualifies that the forbidden intercourse meant is that which is forbidden due to lack of ownership of pleasure (like zina), not temporary prohibitions. Several cases illustrate the principle: wati' of a son's slave-girl does not lead to hadd for qadhf because it is not zina; wati' of a Magian slave-girl does not remove ihsan because ownership is full; wati' of a slave-girl that the father wati'a or wati' of a foster-sister removes ihsan because the prohibition is perpetual. A key ikhtilaf is narrated: if a man touches or looks with desire at a slave-girl's mahram and then wati'a her, Abu Hanifa holds that ihsan remains (accuser is liable), while the Sahibayn hold that ihsan is removed (accuser not liable). The conclusion from Sharh at-Tahawi summarizes: zina, shubha, nikkah fasid, or wati' of a perpetually prohibited person removes ihsan; other wati' (like during menstruation, or with full ownership) does not.

Key Terms
ملك المتعة (milk al-mut'a): Ownership of the right to sexual pleasure, which a man has over his slave-girl or wife.
وطء بشبهة (wat' bi shubha): Intercourse under a mistaken belief of legality, e.g., marrying a woman believed to be lawful but actually unlawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the ruling on a man who wati'a his Magian slave-girl?
A) His ihsan is removed, and his accuser is not subject to hadd.
B) His ihsan is not removed, and his accuser is subject to hadd.
C) The ruling depends on whether the qadif is Muslim.
D) His ihsan is removed only if he wati'a her repeatedly.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan for qadhf is removed only by intercourse that is zina in nature (lacking full ownership of pleasure) or with a perpetually prohibited person; temporary prohibitions do not affect it.
